O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles of medical science and its explanations, and have finished it with its interpretations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of surgery, that is to say "surgery."
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the practice of surgery is forbidden in our region and is banned altogether, the science has perished and been cut off, and there remains nothing of it outside of the small descriptions in books by ancient authors that have been handled by hands (i.e., used).
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And it is because of this that errors and falsehoods have arisen, and the intentions have been clouded over and knowledge has been driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and the other instruments of the craft along with the description and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled craftsmen of hands can be found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who engages in this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they may know the members (of the body) accurately, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and arteries, and the number of them, and the function of those that move and those that rest, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates said that "the name is much, and the thing (or the reality) is little"; and it is the same in the art of surgery or manual craft.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things, let him beware that he does not fall into error and kill men; just as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck and cut the arteries of her neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another physician who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large, but he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they operated on him, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see one other physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound to the splints with great force, and leaves no bandage on the wound, but instead leaves it exposed; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg swelled up completely and the foot became necrotic.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind his leg; and when I had undone it, he was relieved and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But the corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the member was entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who lanced a boil that had become cancerous, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in a place where one can completely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: namely, work in which there is danger in many ways; and I will point out in every section of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take up your weapons in earnestness and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you come to safety and are praised; and leave behind incurable diseases with great care; and put aside your doubts and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of serious illnesses, lest you be called a foolish fool."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medical cauteries, and the chapter is arranged from head to toe; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools for cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about reducing dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to toe, and with the forms of instruments
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is appropriate for me to say the quality of help and harm of each complexion (temperament).
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest in speech and the most subtle in knowledge and in hidden responses; and of this, many sages spoke and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, a hot complexion without matter and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that the cautery is of great help there; while others have said the opposite: that the cautery is not beneficial for illnesses arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot and should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness, as said by those who claim that the cautery provides great help for hot and dry illnesses affecting the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cool.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And yet, it should not be attempted by anyone other than those who have experienced it and are knowledgeable about the chapter of cauteries, as well as the diversity of human complexions, dispositions, and causes of their ailments, and their outcomes and the seasonal variations; we are not afraid of other complexions, even in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery is among the essential treatments, and of greater goodness than heated medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is being cauterized, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to do so.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Heated medicines spread from member to member, causing illnesses that are difficult to heal and potentially killing the patient in some cases.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	For fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not cause this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of the matter; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the lengthiness of my speech, for I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that lies within fire, and its quality, as well as how it removes illnesses from bodies, just as the philosopher states in his demonstrations. Now receive this in your thoughts.[Comment: This passage suggests that the author is a practitioner who has gained knowledge through experience and study, and he values the effectiveness of fire-based treatments. He wants to share his findings but also preserve their secrecy and the power they hold in healing illnesses.]
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and they chose priests.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that a cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm caused by an affliction is reduced by the aid of a cautery; and even when the cautery is necessary to alleviate urgent and severe pain that cannot wait for greater damage to occur to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish doctors do; for there is no return of the disease that is healed by cautery; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not just any medicine that changes the complexion, but rather dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is valuable for its speed and for the power of its action and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	It is possible that the disease sometimes comes according to the complexion of the patient and the location and strength of the disease; and the excesses accumulate in him through the acquisition of food and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there are few excesses and moisture, such as dens cauteries for pain, and similar things. And this type of pain does not return, but it is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "derrière" (hindering) of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cautery can be effective after medical treatment, but their belief is false. The term "cautery is the derrière of medicine" means that when we administer methods of cures for any illness and they are not effective, we then administer cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is the "derrière" (hindering) of medicine, but not in the way foolish physicians understand it to be.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they only claimed this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not become necrotic, but that is not true, as I have experienced. However, I have found that cautery with gold is indeed more effective than iron, just as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot be sure when it is hot enough because of the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down. If it is heated too much, it will become brittle in the fire, which presents a significant challenge.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to foot, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moistness and coldness in the brain, and there are two that are made for a disease called "soda" (tension headache), and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for an abundance of dreams, pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis and cramp and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine, loosening the head three or four nights, depending on what the virtue and the water and the habit of the patient can bear; and then let the patient's head be shaved.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something firm; then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come, bleed slightly, then heat the cautery called "olivare," of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make a small puncture while pulling downward and outward with your hand; then quickly remove your hand and check the mark to see if you see a small hole; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a pinch of salt and put it in warm water and soft cotton inside, and place it on the wound, and leave it for three days; then apply a damp cloth soaked in butter and leave it on until the burn is healed; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and therefore it heals faster.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that the cautery should be left on long enough that part of the bone is burned, and then what has been burnt of the bone should be scraped off and treated.[](Note: This treatment may seem barbaric by modern standards. Medical practices in medieval times were often based on superstition and limited knowledge of anatomy and infection. The use of cautery was a common practice, but it could also lead to complications such as infection or excessive scarring.)
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that one should leave the cautery for a while, and apply it strongly enough that it leaves a mark as wide as a finger ring that women wear on their thimbles, so that the humors may come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should clean and suture it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every case, except in certain men where there is a dangerous condition; and it seems to me that I should leave the other method; for the head is weakened by continuous loosening through natural means, as we have witnessed in other limbs; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healthy and effective for me, I use this method to bring about a cure.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain comes to the whole head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and oils and poultices; and if one applies the cautery as we have said before, but it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head (chiefly referring to the shoulder area in this medical context) is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize it a little below the fire cautery we mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterward, perform cautery on each horn of the head (referring to the temples) up to the bone, as we mentioned before, and make a "vasel" shaped cautery mark at the spot; it is a blister in which cups are placed. Keep your hand light so that you do not touch the bone. The patient will feel more significant pain in this cautery than in others, but I will speak of that later. It is important that the cauteries on the horns be finer than those used for the middle of the head; this is the method:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery on the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in a part of the head and the illness extends up to the eye, and the head has been purged by cleansing medicines, and other cures as I mentioned in the division of diseases have been attempted without success, then cautery should be performed in two ways: with medication and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medical practice of cautery consists of taking a twig of alder, removing the bark and soaking it in a mixture of two parts ground herbs. Then make an incision in the temple where the pain lies, in such a way that the alder twig can be placed under the skin. Once placed, bind and press it tightly for twelve hours, then remove it and leave the wound open for two or three days before applying a compress soaked in butter to promote healing.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment has healed, and if you wish to use any of the burning medicines I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is done in this manner. Heat the cautery to a degree as shown in the following form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the tip is shaped like a bell with one small indentation in the middle. Place it on the painful area and hold it there while moving it slightly for a short period of time until half of the tip's thickness has been burnt. Then lift your hand so that the artery, which is located further away from the burn, does not get burned, allowing for an abundant flow of blood to leave the body.[^1^]
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, put cotton in the wound covered with silk, and leave it on for three days; then put wet cotton smeared with butter, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this pimple with the cautery called "cultellare," at the whole tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this pimple which is not old.
de emigraine	of a pimple or swelling.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure a pimple or swelling as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery before described with medicine and iron is not enough, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is red; and pass it lightly over the painful place a line of half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and draw back so as not to cover the artery and not reach the bone; and watch out for the jaw that moves when one chews, and the nerve does not move, and that spasms do not come upon the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear, even for those who do not know about it, and who are not trained and experienced; and leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how to stop blood flow when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it fits in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is strong, cauterize it in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and medical treatments and other cures as we have mentioned in the division have been tried but the pain persists, then heat this "pointed" cautery, of which the form is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, point all around the affected ear, or both ears if the pain is in both, and move back a bit from the root of the ear after making a mark; and have ten "points" around each ear; then heal the area until it is healed.[Welcome to the help desk! de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture (pain) that should be treated with cautery is only those that are caused by an excess of fluids, as we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cautery to similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture that moves with fluid from bodily purges and head cleansings and rinses, and if it is not effective, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; place the cautery on the healthy-looking part, and burn the patient near the top of the ear, a little below the ear horn, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the appearance of the knife that we mentioned before is similar, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a bit larger; after treating the wound as I have said before, until it heals completely.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said before, but it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the side called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	The word "litargie" in medieval medical texts usually refers to a type of paralysis or loss of movement in a part of the body, often affecting the face or limbs. It is derived from the Greek word "lethargia," which means "forgetfulness" or "sleepiness." A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large quantities of grains and cleansing pills for the brain; then shave the patient's head and apply the plaster of sinapis (mustard seed) to the back of the head, as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: perform it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it (the abscess) is cleaned out in this way, that is good; and if not, perform three cauterizations on the head, starting from the crown and going down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cauterization; and treat it as you would other wounds, and if you see fit and the patient can tolerate it, perform one cauterization in the middle (of the abscess); and if necessary, two others on the two ends (of the abscess), and continue treatment until it is healed; and use the type of cauterization called "olivare," as I have mentioned before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the chill/coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed with grains and the other things we have mentioned before; then shave the patient's head and perform cauterization on the head and on each horn (temple), and one at the back and three along the spine of the neck; and if necessary, and the body is moist and the patient can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, perform four cauterizations along the spine of the back; and leave it alone until the hottest part of the heat (of the cauterization) has subsided, then remove your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and use the type of cauterization called "olivare," which we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of yellowness and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, have them gargle and chew food that purifies the brain frequently with good meats; then let blood from the middle of the head, and perform one cautery according to what we have said before, and one cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able to endure it, perform cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, perform one subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, superfluities or corrupt moisture cause thick phlegm, then use such hot irons as we have said for someone with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities tend towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify the brain, as mentioned in the previous division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, shave the patient's head; then make a well-made linen compress in the shape of a circle and place it on their head; have the patient lie crosswise and ensure they are well-restrained from all sides; then apply the liniment and warm it with moderately hot fire, so that the heat can be tolerated when applied to the head; then remove the circle from inside the head and let it cool; and do this for the patient once a week with other good treatments until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or, if you wish to cauterize the patient by making multiple punctures with the entire cautery. This method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; and then place a cotton pad soaked in butter and gelatin on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyelid(s)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyelid swells for the first time with the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something cleansing for the head and guarding against all moistures, and make him sweat or take baths several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, order the patient to tilt their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the swelling of the eyelid is on both eyes together, or on one if it is only on one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skin for the entire length of the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for blood flow, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as well as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making incisions, how to stop them with caution; and sometimes cautery or a hot iron is done under the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids of phlegm, then perform the cautery that I have said at the beginning of the eye treatment: one cautery in the middle of the forehead, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the hollows below the two bones; and if more is needed, cauterize it profusely above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	within the body of tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the sick person three roasted chickpeas to drink; after that, apply a cautery to the middle of the head with an olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the eyebrows, slightly below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the eye has been softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery, which is called "olivary," of which the following is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the paper has been burned, according to the method that I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that points to the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It sometimes happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and then cauteries are made in two ways: either by fire or by a burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the eyelashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on a piece of paper place an image that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and pearl powder on the eye, then heat the cautery to the shape described here:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing near the mark that you have made many times, so that the skin is burnt there; and the sign of a successful procedure is seeing the paper retracted and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days. Then apply moist cotton until the burn is healed; after that, treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then reapply the cautery to the same spot as before, just as you did at first; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises up to its natural position, and is even, and do not cause any pain to the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fiery medical cautery is what you should instruct the patient to do, letting their hairs grow long and even until they are full-grown; then make a form from parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and work quickly so that it does not cool down. Spread this mixture on the form as if it were a fern leaf, and place it on the paper over the eyes. If the illness affects only one eye, then you should work on just one, and if in both eyes, do the same; and place moist cotton beneath the affected eye, using egg white. The patient's head should be in your care, and place your hand over the medicine, pressing once every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, for they will feel it as if it were fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from its case.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting (insect) has passed, lift the cloth and check if you see the skin stretched as if it had been stretched by heat or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the cloth until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then place a wet cotton compress soaked in butter over the burnt area until the burn has cooled down. Afterwards, cure the wound dressing called "dyafenis" and others until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to be careful with your work and ensure that no medicine drips into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft, and hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area where the skin has softened, just as you did before; after that, cure it until it is healed. This is the method for treating an inflamed eye:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this should be your constraints; and do not apply the same treatment to everyone, as the study of this art requires.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on them in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or deviate; then apply a cotton swab soaked with egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat up the cautery tool which is parted: and attach it to the head so that it forms like the shape of a dove's feather quill, bring the two ends together so that they meet, and if you wish, sharpen it from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it curved like a tent; but in any case, this tool is useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and extract the rotten tissue and pus from it; and if it is closed, incise it and extract the contents; then place hot bran on top of the cautery tool, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the eye so that your hand does not move excessively; and apply the cautery to the fatty tissue of the eyelid and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good. If not, then perform cautery again and as many times as necessary, leaving it for three days; then place a cotton swab soaked in butter on top of it, and treat the inflammation until it is healed; and if 40 days have passed and it has not yet healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and refer to what comes next in the chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a kind of fire cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and break the opening; then place in the split a thin probe of such material as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the quantity of a thumb's width; and hold your hand firmly on the probe, ensuring that the patient does not move at all, lest the melted lead flows into their eye; and it is necessary to place over the patient's eye a piece of damp cotton soaked in egg white or oil: the lead will draw out the pus from the fistula with marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, that is good. If not, one must administer a puncture to the abscess and return the fistula to the body of the abscess as appropriate in its specific location.
des crevaices en levres	of ruptures on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear on lips that are called "wrinkles," and similarly on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have mentioned in divisions, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small scalpel-shaped fire cautery of this shape:

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and burst and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have mentioned in divisions, but it does not improve: then you need to use a cautery according to the size of the fistula; place the probe or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and behind the opening; and do this once or twice, after treating it as we have mentioned in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated this way, it is good; but if not, then you must uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find it in its chapter.[Note: The original text uses "cautere" which means a hot iron or scalpel, while the term "fer chaud" in the translated text means "hot iron". dou movement des dens	from movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but it is of no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its shape will be as described later, with a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and hold it for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the moisture is corrupted and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether it is real or imagined, and medical treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to use the cautery in two ways: with butter cautery and fire cautery.[ next line ]
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and soak it in boiled butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it cools down; and do this often until the virtue of the butter reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see it necessary, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which the shape will come after, and place it on the tooth while holding your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be relieved on the same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in preparation for this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery to any part of the head that you want and as you have power; and this is the shape of the rod:
des scrophules	Of scrofula. Scrofula is a form of tuberculosis that affects the lymph nodes in the neck, causing them to become swollen and inflamed. It was a common ailment during medieval times. The text suggests using cautery as a treatment for scrofula. The fire cautery would be applied to the affected area of the neck, with the patient holding still to prevent movement and potentially worsening the condition. The butter cautery would also be used, in which boiled butter is soaked into cotton or wool and placed on the affected area to reduce pain and inflammation. This treatment was likely used in conjunction with other medical practices, such as herbal remedies and bloodletting.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulous swellings are due to phlegm and cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-steel so as to produce the following form, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side away from the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, as needed, until it reaches the base of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply a cautery in proportion to its size, and leave it on for three days; then apply a wet cotton compress soaked in butter until the burn is healed; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moistures have conquered the channels of the peritoneum, and also when it is due to a cold complexion, then the patient should first be emptied with resolving medicines; after that, cauterize at the base of the throat, but take care not to come all the way to the throat, and only burn slightly, not from the heart. Then perform another cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, using a "clavile" cautery, of which we have previously given the form; and treat the area as previously described until it is healed.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	about the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries.

And if it is dislocated above, what happens but little, then perform fire cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or with many cauteries when pricking. dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy with aristolochia roots, and in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and hold it in the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the area that is beneath the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a little behind; and one in the armpit, and one on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest beyond the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but instead make it open as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And some ancients said that certain people use a fire cautery similar to a razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if done correctly, the pain goes away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die or that a fistula will come which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or mites)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the "mice" (or mites) in those that I have mentioned in the divisions of cures, and it does not help at all, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	One of these ways is to make three or four cauteries in a row, following the length of the "mice" (or mites), following the shape of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back;[

And another way of cautery is to heat the one that has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the chest which is opposite the "mice" (or mites), where the patient's ribs come towards the left, and let the lifting of the chest be according to the chest, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	Afterwards, put in the two inflamed nerves until the chest is pierced from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four (cauteries). And if you wish, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves. Afterwards cure when it has cast off pus for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy (a historical term for edema, or swelling due to an accumulation of fluid in the body)
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The cautery is not beneficial for the hydropsy patient, except for the method called "asclytes". When you cure them according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, two behind the back along the spine, and one near the side; and let the cauteries be close to the thick part of the kidney.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery to smolder for a long time, and do not stop the care of the patient after the cautery; and if healing is hurried, the two intentions will come together with the help of God. de l’enfleure des piez	of inflammation of the feet
