And if you see excessive moisture and the patient suffering, perform cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries next to the large one on the stomach, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Here is a line-by-line translation of the provided Old French text about the treatment of hemorrhoids:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old, and are large cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions, but without success, then perform cauteries: three on the spine of the back, this one being entirely outside below the dimple, and one cautery under each buttock.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that their stomach is cold and food does not cook, and the face appears swollen, then perform a large cautery on the stomach as previously mentioned, and another one on the liver, and another one on the spleen with all the cautery clavicle; and leave the cautery open for a long time. Afterward, care for the area until it is healed.[Combined all translations into one.]
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy part which is called "thigh"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thigh, heat the fire-brand that looks like a razor, and then place it all glowing hot on the cut thigh; leave your hand there until the brand reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of flesh, cauterize each part as we have said; after that, use wound-healing treatments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large fire-brand made of alum, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate surgery or incision (which we will discuss later), then there comes a disease that can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes to someone, and it is mature and casts rottenness and corrupt humors, you should test it with a thin probe, and make sure that you know the depth of the probe entirely. Afterwards, heat the cautery which looks like a razor, and put it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and reheat the cautery until the rotten and corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of flesh needing to be removed; and take care not to burn the nerves which are inside, and the large veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, beware of these areas, and do not make cuts outside of the fleshy area, and consider that it is not persistent; after healing the area until it is healed, and if the area protrudes, and the contents are removed for a long time, then know that the area is fully healed; and if the contents are not removed, know that the area is full, and the bone at the base is rotten; and thus one of these as we shall say in its place.

Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac. And if these cauteries are not present, make three cauteries of large olives, and let the cauteries be as deep as all hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	for hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the joint of the hip, and it is caused by coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of heavy humors with stinking pills, or other good similar ones.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, perform cauterization; and the methods of cauterization are of two kinds: that is to say, hot medicinal irons, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the joint of the swelling three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a deep and large wound between each cautery the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is done in the middle on top of the swelling, so that there are four in total according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we previously mentioned for the dislocation of the swelling; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire swelling, and all the flesh around the edge is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are done where the patient indicates that the pain is, and one circular cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cauteries be of a knife-like shape, and let the flesh around the edge be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends down to the bones of the foot or near it, then cauterize there where they feel the pain three or four times with the pointed cautery that is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, more are done; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a knife-like or circular cautery is done, and be careful in all your cauteries to not leave the cautery on for so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and the foot as well, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. Afterwards, they died from a stomach ailment.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on both, following this method. // And the wise men said in the cautery for inflammation, of which this is the method, make a iron that is as thick as a thumb's width of dactyl (a unit of measurement), or just a bit less, and it should be interlaced, and let there be a space between the interlacings equal to the size of a nut; and let the interlacings be turned two ways, and let them be like knots, and let there be one handle of iron well-made; and this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one application of the iron, leaving it for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery due to fear of its appearance, and there are few who use it; but it is one of the good cauteries for those who can tolerate it, and where it is applied.[IMPRESSION]
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or being struck, or from excessive bleeding, or from the spreading of cold matter, none of these instances is appropriate for cauterization, except in the case of one caused by the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or similar treatments, three lines be signed on the back, in the area where the pain is located, using incense; and within each line, five cauterizations or more should be made, depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauterization be done using the type of cauterization called "poins"; and if you wish, make three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien technique, in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have stiff necks when they get up, and fear; and you will find on the last spine in the back, and the appearance which comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see these signs and wish to cure them, cauterize with the cautery of this type, in this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine equally. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine using the cautery, making two or three lines, and have the points close to one another. Afterwards heal the area until it is healed, as we have said, and beware not to apply cautery to gout that is in a nerve spasm.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture spread throughout the entire body, and when it occurs in the feet, which is called "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be treated with cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let them be olive-shaped, as follows:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if necessary, make the cautery on the sole of the foot with the entire surface of the cauterizing instrument, which is called "point." And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, which happens often, make three or four cauteries on each knee, in every part, with the entire olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not keep your hand there for too long that the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines long; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and have them take medicines. For if you take good care of them and purge fluids, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the opening of the abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see to cure it, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that empty the belly, so that the feces descend from their belly; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has receded, and press gently with your fingers around the abscess on the bone of the wrist, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [Here a picture/diagram would follow in the original text]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	...until it is white and exudes pus. Then press the bowels back into place; and have the attendant place their hand so that they do not return; and work well the thighs of the patient, and place beneath them one cushion and one sergeant on the thighs, and another on the chest who holds their hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it firmly and long enough to reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you come to the bone; and pay close attention so that the abscess does not burst when you apply the cautery, so that you do not burn them, and so that through this the patient does not die or suffer further harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are in vain. And it is necessary for the cauteries of children to be fine according to the measure of eggs, and also for adults as large according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after curing other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the bubbles do not burst when he gets up in chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and carry it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he moves little and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and loud talking; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of abdominal surgery
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures (hernias) occur in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform one cautery with the reusable cautery according to its size, and let a third of the belly be burned; after that, cure as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the three-pronged cautery in this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but sign first the joint's location and make a mark along the width above the rupture, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire fire-brand. But the first cautery is lighter and swifter.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a member because of a fall or injury and that pain lasts for a long time and medical treatment is ineffective, then it is necessary that the area be cauterized with the "point" cautery, and let the cautery match the length of the member, its size, weakness, and power, as well as its location and level of pain. If the wound heals from the first cautery, that's good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for sometimes it is necessary to change the location of the cautery on the body part, therefore one must perform cauteries until the patient heals.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from the putrefaction of humours and melancholy. When you see a patient to be cauterized, pay attention if the disease is at its beginning and if it has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen or linger, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, another towards the front at the end of the hairline; and two on the temples, and one at the back near the nape; and leave your hand there long enough for the cautery to reach the bone, and until the scabs come out, so that the vapors of the foul humours can escape; and cauterize on the skin according to what it looks like before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the diseased place is spread out everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the following cauteries that we have mentioned in the head: one cautery on the nose, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the hip and another next to it, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the knees of the legs, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are at the back of the heel so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Know that the more you do cautery, the more help you provide and the more it benefits the patient; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already corrupt. And you should make the cautery big or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the ways of irons. After the cure, dust the wound with flour of vetch and honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	"of inflammation" or "swelling"
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines, oils, and plasters, yet it is not healed, then cautery is done on the limb according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep in the flesh; then cure it with dressings until it is healed. And sometimes cautery is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the opening of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should intervene if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the openings of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	I'm not sure what you're asking. The term "de albaras" does not appear in the Old French medical text provided earlier. Could you please clarify your request or provide more context? I'll be happy to help further.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become advanced and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the size of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a rooster and pigeon, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer (or more accurately, "chancre") by cautery refers to the use of hot metal instruments to burn or destroy diseased tissue. This was a common medical practice in medieval times due to the lack of effective surgical techniques and anesthetics. Here's a possible line-by-line translation:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre begins and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, using the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot grow
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in growing or due to the excess fluid it makes, or due to the water of the patient if they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its growth: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; then leave it like that. Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this: (followed by a description of shaping the cautery)
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the core, and such that the cauteries are felt from outside in such a way that the course of the rotting is eased. Afterward, cure it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	There is another kind of disease called "corrodens," which is nothing but an eating away of the member, for it consumes the members just like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cautery along with fire, then heat the cauteries, small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing remain of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it alone for three days, and put on poultices with oil on the cauterized places until the burns from the fire are healed, and all of the corruption. Afterward, cure it with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places. And this eating away has sometimes been cured by medicinal agents instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for medicinal agents in the division: take them when you need them.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the corns that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often happens that in the feet a sickness is born which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscessed thing that wounds the foot. And the cauteries for this sickness are of two kinds. That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is when you heat up a probe-like lancet as big as a roof beam, made of good iron, measured so it can touch the nail from all sides, and having sharp edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until you reach the base of the nail; and leave it like that for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster of crushed marsh mallow with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound with a cleansing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by moisture in the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this way: take a rod of iron or copper, or a probe-like lancet, and place it on the nail and the stylet, that is to say, porrelly verrucae; and place the rod on top so that it heats up all around, then add some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edges of the rod come to the root of the nail, and can find a deep path through the hot water to the root; and have the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will uproot all its roots. Do this one after another, until you reach all those in the body, then cure the wounds with cleansing ointments that cause flesh to grow.
li cure dou trembler	I would translate "li cure dou trembler" as "the treatment for trembling".
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from cold nerves or quartan fever or other causes, then you should make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one in the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive cautionery; this will stop the trembling, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of smelly pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes appear on the body, due to a lack of bathing, or smelly pustules that come from corrupt matter. It is necessary, when they first appear, to apply cautery to each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made of myrtle wood, with its tip taken by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or of the lenticular cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but rather the excess is broken up from which they come, and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is great loss of blood from the artery which is cut in the wound, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop [the bleeding].
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, hurry to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips from it; then heat various olive-shaped cauteries, both large and small, until they are all red; then take one, whether large or small, according to the size and location of the wound in which the artery is cut, and place the cautery on this vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another one quickly from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and take care not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood runs from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is through one of the four ways that we have said: through cauterization, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	One who will administer stopping the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not help much.[Original text is in Medieval French, and I am providing a translation into Modern English.]
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone who does not have any remedy or medicine present, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it stops bleeding over the wound and over the vein; and they must not move it, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on fevers from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter along the same path so that one may more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this one, it is important, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake foolish things. For many kinds of people come to be cured, some of whom are so afflicted with their illness that they easily die due to the severity and greatness of its malice; and one should fear for these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these, there are some who claim to be healed and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the illness is deceitful. It is not at all appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than into your greed. Do not rashly but wisely open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you to establish a good reputation, and glory, and memories of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, May our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe in the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have arranged this chapter for you, dividing it into sections according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have described from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a swollen head filled with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the womb constrains the child's head too forcefully; and sometimes it happens for no known reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death came quickly; and for this reason, it seems to me that it would be better to abandon such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child in whom the head was filled with water, and the head grew heavier each day until it could no longer be supported; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture is collected under the bone above the hip, between the pelvis and the bone. The treatment for this condition is as follows if the moisture is between the pelvis and the bone, and the abscess is small: make an incision in the head, wide enough to allow the moisture to drain out; it should be at least two fingers long, depending on where the moisture is located. Here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, as shown below:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the chin spread apart from each other in every part, and fluid comes out when you press it with your hand from the inside, and this does not heal: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision, remove all of the moisture. Then bind the incisions with cloth and powders, and apply wine and oil, leaving it like this until the fifth day; then undo it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and also leave the head bound, and give the patient dry food and little liquid until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe where the swelling of the abscess appears and the gathering of water, for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut there where the abscess is visible and the gathering of water, in a manner according to your ability; and be careful not to cut the artery; and if blood flows from it, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of a rupture (or swelling)
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a person becomes ill with a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or the feet, and the illness is chronic and not helped by medical treatment, then the last resort is the fire cautery; this will involve burning two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you are about to cauterize, the patient should turn their head; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries become visible, next have the patient stretch their neck over a single cloth; then look for where the veins bulge and the locations of the two arteries are near the ears and protrude; mark those locations with ink, and then cut both arteries with a sharp spatula in two parts so that the incision reaches the bone and this should be done over the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see (that) the artery, place the sharp spatula under it and cut above it, making two incisions crosswise, like a pair of dice.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will spurt out continuously.[ISI] Et se tu voes que il en sant pas assez, puis esforce le col du malaide au dela de l’espaule et si li frotte le chief et les espaules a un drapel ardant; et se ceo ne li valt riens, si copes la grant artère qui est entre les deux espaulx.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not open to the touch, you should measure a quantity of three fingers' width, then make an incision down to the bone; and the amount of blood that needs to be let is six
de emigrainne	"de grains" in this context likely refers to small grains or seeds. A possible interpretation could be "six grains," which would indicate a measurement of volume, similar to how one might use rice or lentils as a unit of measurement today. However, it is not clear what specific type of grain is meant by "de emigrainne" in this medieval medical text.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When there is an old chronic headache and acute catarrh, caused by moisture in the tears and heat in the temples, and a swollen and insane forehead and similar things, and this condition has been treated with various medical cures without success, then we should draw blood from the temples and cauterize the area. This is what we have described before.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method for extracting the blood from the temples is as follows: the patient should part their hair and pay attention to the artery that is visible in the temple, which can easily be felt due to its pulsating movement. This artery is not very prominent in some people who are too cold; if it is not prominent, the patient should constrict their neck with a cloth, then rub the area with a rough cloth until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take a lancet (spatumile) of the following shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with hemostats, and carefully separate it from the membranes that are beneath it in each part; and if the artery is fine, then hook it with the tip of the uncinate, then cut that part according to the quantity of the two holes. For if it is not cut, the blood will not exit properly at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and draw blood from the six holes, up to three; and if the artery is large, then it must be tied in two places with a sturdy double thread of silk, so that no rotting occurs before the wound heals and proper bleeding takes place; then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the wound with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the holes are closed; and this is the best practice, if the patient does not have a fever and they have a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery stops moisture: therefore it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the area with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; and when they are loosened, they must be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth, and bandages, until it heals; and if a piece of the artery is left as long as you work, then quickly cover it with a cauterizing iron, or fill the area with vitriol and press on it with your hand until the blood stops flowing; and if you don't have that present, then place your finger on the area until the blood clots, and sprinkle cold water on the area until it stops flowing, and press as needed; and the best and easiest method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the wound with this cutting cautery of two parts, but let the edges be thick so that they retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a gap of the width of a thumb between the two blades, and when you have marked the two places to be cauterized, place the red-hot iron on it until it reaches the bone and cut the vein in two places; and keep them separate between the two edges because this cautery is not solid all around; and that is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears come from the veins above the forehead and are not relieved by any medical treatment, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feel a pulsation on the forehead as if it is trembling; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the paper has been warmed up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called it "cure contuse", and it consists of shaving the patient's hair on the forehead, then making three equal incisions on the forehead according to its length; one of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, going down to the eyebrows, and the other two should be above the eyebrows near the temples, taking care not to cut any blood vessels that are located near the eyebrows. Keep your hand away from the jawline, and make each wound the width of three fingers across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth to wipe away the blood, then apply the styptic made of two parts of which this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision made above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts down to the suture on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this styptic.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	and insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellarie", which is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is blunt and not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place the sharp edge of the instrument towards the fleshy part of the flesh and the blunt side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. Cut all the veins that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to where the flesh appears, then make another cut in the middle incision until the other second one; and remove the blood equally, and press the area to extract the blood; then place a piece of old cotton in each incision, and place wet cloths on them with wine, oil, and vinegar, and ensure that no pus forms; and on the third day, loosen the ligament and apply a large amount of hot water, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other treatments used for wound care, until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting catarrh, and you see thin and small eyes, weakened vision, and burnt paper; and the hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that those matters and those catarrhs do not come out but from many veins, and the proper cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is recommended that you instruct the patient to lean their forehead back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead and another one of about an inch. Start from the left temple to the right temple, cutting until you reach the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves near the temples that move while eating. Once the bone is exposed, wipe all blood with a sponge, then separate the two sides of the incision and place old cotton in between, and bandage it with linen cloths. Then bind wet cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, making sure not to cause a hot abscess; once removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying agents that help generate flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner, take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; administer it on these wounds to help generate flesh all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or animals, or mineral stones such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something falls into the ear, such as a stone or other object that does not stick to or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, apply a little drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then facilitate extraction; make them sneeze using condiments, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold the ear upward. Often, this cure will cause it to come out; and if it does not come out, facilitate extraction using subtle pincers, of which this is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out using pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a thin probe wire of fine double-wire. And if it does not come out this way, make a small horn of tin and place the end of the horn in the ear hole, and stop up what is around the horn with soft wax so that no air can enter with the horn; then pull hard, as often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime and apply some to an instrument made for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out using any of the things we have mentioned, then hurry to lance the ear so that abscess and hardening may occur, as well as spasm; and the manner of lancing is such that you should first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty tissue or flesh; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, coming to the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck it out with your mouth; and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot go out, then use a thin spatula of this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision on the grain. But do not do so when you think that the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine tweezers and a succorer, as we have said, in such a way that the extraction is made easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Therefore, in the water that falls into the ear, the patient should use expectoration of condiments first and fill the ear with soft cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by itself, that's good. If not, then take many small and light pebbles, heat them a little by the fire, and have the patient place one in their ear and jump on one foot from the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out. And if you wish, then take a reed and put one end into the ear, and burn the other end with fire until the thicker part of the reed is burned; then repeat this process with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said in the previous method with stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division (?); but if it is of large size that can be felt, then administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure is not effective, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if you see any visible worms, then carefully remove them with tweezers, and if you don't see any, then take a probe of the kind described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow below and wide above. Insert the slender tip of the probe into the ear according to the patient's discomfort level, then push the entire probe firmly; repeat this process until all the worms come out. If they do not obey and come out, then plug cotton around the probe as I have said in the previous section. If they still do not emerge as we have described, then administer the distillations that the ancients have proven to work in the treatment of worms, which you can find in the treatment of distillations; then pour your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument as shown:
