Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or bronze, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation; and have a well-made bronze instrument to press the distillation inside, and if you wish, take a spoon and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you want in the cannula, while keeping it inside the ear; then insert the spoon with all the cotton, and gently press your hand until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; let the patient feel the sensation inside, and let the distillation be a small pot heated by fire so that it can be distilled in the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, as the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	"de l'estoupement des oreilles" means "on ear stoppers/plugs". The term refers to the act of blocking or stopping up the ears, typically by inserting a piece of cotton or other material to prevent air or fluid from entering or escaping. This technique can be used for various purposes, such as protecting the ears during bathing, diving, or flying, relieving ear pain due to changes in pressure, or preventing water from entering the ear canal and causing infection. In a medieval medical context, ear stoppers could also be used in conjunction with distillations or other treatments for the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Any child is born who has no holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from wound or pus inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small hole visible near the hole, and one can see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one then that goes deep, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult healing in many cases, and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary that you expose the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage apparent, work on it immediately with this tool, as described in the following form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is from pus or flesh in the ear, hold it with fine forceps and gently scrape it until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the blockage is deep in the ear, take a fine, light razor, heat it slightly over fire, and then place it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the blockage, and the patient feels pain when hearing, make a small incision carefully, being careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert a wick in the ear according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder on top of vitriol broken; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made of oil rose and wax, as long as the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Here is the translation:
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eye-healing salve that comes in paper when the eyes are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch them with pliers and tweezers, and cut some of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on top of it.[References:](https://www.pinterest.com/pin/547328963015833448/)
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not possible to cut it out, cauterize it with a subtle lenticular cautery, and after the incision, move the cauterizer; and many times they heal, when some things still remain of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burnt and do not return at all.
de la gresle	Of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come onto paper from the eyes small things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "gravel" (translated as "grandine" in Old French), and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the procedure is as follows: take care if the gravel moves from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know; then make an incision of appropriate size, then gently scrape each part, then take it with tweezers and cut it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, attach it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, because the ointment restores it quickly and harms the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and stretch the gravel with tweezers, and cut it and press it from one side and another; and if the paper is separated by incision, it does not harm; and when the gravel is cut, rinse the eye with saline solution, and cure the wound of anything that harms flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that has been smeared on paper sheets and this happens more to children than any other people, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they get a discharge in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and therefore, they lie down on their faces and sleep, and their papers underneath their eyebrows are moist, which makes them swell and have the appearance of exinach that is apparent in the eye. And when you press on the area with your fingers, you can feel the exinach come out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is as follows: the patient places their head over your sanitary place; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach present on each part, then place it on top of it; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a small knife, not wider than the wound made for bloodletting; and cut the leather deep enough to reach the exinach; and in several ways, the exinach comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it with a piece of cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and make sure not to touch the incision, not to reach all the way to the eye, so that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not appear at the beginning of the cut, slightly increase the cut legibly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place it on the wound, and bind it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that has remained, then cure it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the place, then cure it with soothing ointments until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	"of the hairs of papers"
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on papers that are not natural and are old, they harm the eyes and cause various kinds of illnesses such as excessive tearing, softening of the eyelids, and inflammation, to the point that it can lead to eye destruction. And there are four ways to cure this: either by cautery with fire or by a soothing medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cautery, and this can be done through incision and stitching or bandaging, depending on what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle with a thread on it; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and pull one thread above the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, up to the entire width, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then pull one thread and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then sign on the paper a figure like a myrtle leaf, and nonetheless it is necessary that the figure corresponds to the height that you see raised the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a need to cut a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper is; then make an incision on both lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear duct down to the small one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs, as thick as a root, then insert the probe into one of the two angles of the corner, then scrape it all off; then bring the two lips together with a stitch of a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluous threads on both eyebrows adhere to anything sticky, if you want to do so; and if not, then don't worry about it, then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without drying or constricting materials, for the paper will swell with the healing of the wound and bring them together, but the stitches are harmful (as the ancients said), and this is a fearless task.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is another way, it is that you sign the paper with a figure that looks like a myrtle leaf, as we have said before, with three incisions separated according to the shape that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what protrudes with small force equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the strength to hold the pincers and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread and place it in the middle of the wound; and place another thread next to the large notch, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have told; then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if a pustule comes to your incision, soothe it with a compress and similar soothing ointment.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper (scalp) are turned (in growth direction); then you should do as we have said about incisions, but stitches in one and the other are more difficult (to perform).
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of keloids is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper (scalp) and make an incision according to what I have said, and then make two incisions with skill, and two thin threads as long as the paper and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two corners of the two sides where you hold the threads; then join them gently on top of the paper above the eye, and pull the two threads firmly from both sides; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin that is pulled will die, blacken, and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, then cut it with more force, and cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and the paper (scalp) has lifted, and the hairs will no longer prickle; and this is the shape of the two keloids that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine strand of silk; then bring together the edges (of the wound) and tie the threads together gently, and let the length of the threads be a palm's length; then place another fine thread of silk in the groove and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient put his head in your lap; and do this in such a way that the work is well-lit, for it is delicate and fine work; then insert the needle into the root of the hair next to the wound, and make it pass through the paper quickly until you draw it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the groove, and insert the pulled-out hairs into the groove, whether there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that all of the hairs come out at the groove with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the groove is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the groove downwards along the thread that you have placed in it, until the groove comes out of the opening and you can see it with your eye; then you will pull the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hairs stiffen in their place and new flesh grows; and if the hairs are small, then attach a long hair from the natural eyebrows to them, and lift it up with that or leave it alone, until it has become detached and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of eye ulcers (or: of eye rottenness)
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or ulceration occurs in the eye, it can happen in two ways: naturally and unnaturally. It can occur suddenly due to a wound, a cut, or cauterization, and through similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of the treatment is that you split that suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying and constricting substances in the cure of it. Because if you do so, the illness will return worse than before; but use soothing substances, such as fenugreek; and let water or ale and linseed be cooked, and heated oils, and wrap a bandage around it, and cure it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is only a remedy for this disease, so that it does not return to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is beneath (the eye) is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural as well as accidental. The accident comes from wound or incision or cautery or similar things; and the method of treatment for it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come into two parts of the flesh; then stretch the skin above along the entire needle, and cut it with a spatula about an inch wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the form of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits along the edge inside the paper; and let the corners of the two splits be the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make them into two angles so that when they are assembled, the form is like the form of a letter called "J Greek"; then remove the flesh according to the width that its edges are thicker than what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said about mild medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split, stitch or cauterization, then you must make a clean split in the paper under the hairs, and as it is described above; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters must prepare means to the best of their ability how to make the form return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is required of labor and instruments in several dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bonding occurs in many people in such a way that the paper is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, so that you cut what is hard at the thin membrane (spatulum subtile), which should not be too sharp or too thick, so that the patient cannot bear that the spatula is too sharp and wounds the eye; and let your incision, by which you scrape this assembly, be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and let the whole assembly be healed, and do some times in the eye with salty water, and raise it with fresh water and collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a bandage of linen, and place wet wool on the eye with plenty of egg yolk; and after three days use collyrium and other remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the toe of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the toenail can be of two types: it is nerve-like and similar to a hard callus, and another type which is not nerve-like, but rather similar to congealed white moisture. When one touches it with iron and tries to prick it with tweezers, they cannot. And both types begin near the outer corner of the eye, and grow little by little until they cover the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient should place their head over you, then open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand and use tweezers to pull the toenail straight. Then take a needle and put a horsehair, cow hair or buffalo hair on it, along with strong thread. Bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the toenail, piercing it all the way through with the needle. Attach the nail with a piece of thread and stretch it upwards. Then remove the skin next to the root of the nail, including the membrane and soft tissue, until you reach the base of the eyelashes, leaving the natural color or corner of the eye untouched. This way, the normal flow of tears will not be affected by the incision. Sometimes the toenail is only stretched with thread as we have described. The following is the method for removing the entire nail:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to let the soft tissue touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, nor let the pupil be pierced. After making the incision, put a little bit of crushed salt and a collar made from litharge into the eye and leave it there until the next day. Then cure the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this similar condition of a nail is often cured with medical treatments; and they arise as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye look at it, and take the spatula, lightly hooked, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully retract the nail above, and if you see that it does not become thinner and the swelling approaches, distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red-colored and boiled oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no obstacle is present in the eye, such as an abscess, then lactate it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh in the eyelid is harmful to the eye due to great injury, then suspend it with a suture, and remove part of it and not all of it, so that there is no accumulation of tears; then distill red collyrium made of litharge into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Sometimes a red flesh is born in men's eyes, covering the pupil and pressing on the membranes, turning them outwards, appearing like a rose of baluster; and the procedure is that the patient places his head over your sanction, then you open their eyes, and pull all that flesh with suitable tweezers, holding it tight; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the end, but be careful not to wound the eye during the process; and let the incision be made with a scalpel as we mentioned in the incision of the nail and small splinters that are removed, just as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, apply eye medication consisting of crushed herbs or red bile and similar corrosive medicines, then place cotton with egg white on the eye outside to ensure it is kept away from hot abscess; if anything remains and pus accumulates and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with calming agents until it heals, then return to your work once the eye has healed. Repeat this process whenever flesh grows back in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is important to lighten the treatment of each weak eye by natural means and for accidental causes with surgery; and do not rush into any of these procedures before you see that this limb can withstand the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that are located over the eye and interfere with its function and weaken it every day. Therefore, it is necessary at first to check if the eyeball is in its place, and if there is no other disease but sebel; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently draw those veins to their full length according to your knowledge, and let the incisions be fine double in this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees in one body in this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully extract those veins and wipe the blood away hour by hour until you see the red veins moving outside of the eye; and be careful not to poke the eye with the tip of the spatula, and perform this procedure at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut more than the veins; and when you have done this, instill a mixture of green and red bile into the eye to dissolve any remaining sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to extract all of it in that hour, make a plaster for the eye with calming ingredients to alleviate eye pain and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and any risk of infection has passed; then continue with the previous method until the eye is healed. This is the shape of the forces (treatment):
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The experts call a fistula of the eye an "arissati": when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it: you need to make an incision on the abscess, where it should burst, and drain all the pus that is in it until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all the instruments that I have described; and it is called an "aspre chief", and should be made of iron in the shape of a rounded head, and sharpened like a file as shown in the following form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the "aspre chief" on the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press down firmly until you feel that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the layer of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the layer is solidified and flesh has grown, and the flesh of the wound is solidified and remains in this state for 40 days without becoming inflamed or experiencing any adverse effects, then you can be sure that it is healed. If not, there is no other solution but to return the fistula to the opening of the nose by exposing the bone a second time with iron, and using hot medicines. When it is exposed, take a "foret" shaped as shown in this form, and make the head of the metal piece have three angles, and taper the handle down to a point as you can see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it next to the bone near the cheekbone, and move your hand away from the eye by about a finger-width, then turn the drill until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of breath escaping if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened in the area, the matter will go to the nose; this makes it an easier task for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide and there is no disturbance or decrease in vision, then bind the patient, then cleanse it, then apply suction cups or leeches without striking, then place a bandage made of vinegar, aloe, incense, and sarcocola on the eye, and then strain the eye and dress it with compresses and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is to take soft cloths, folded in four layers, and then place one upon the other according to the quantity needed for the eye; then bind it tightly with a sturdy bandage, and reapply the suction cups without striking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the bandage weakens, strain it very much; then remove the bandage after a day and night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good; if not, continue with the dressing and cloths and bandage until it has healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a detached retina.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the grown-together flesh, it becomes visible and comes out like a piece of resin from paper; then, if you see such a sight, the procedure is as follows: insert a needle into the root of the lower part all the way to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the eyelid; make it go through and leave the first needle in place according to its position. Then cut the loose end of the double thread and tie one end of the eyelid around it, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth soaked in egg yolk on it. Leave it until the thread dries out with the eye, then cure the eye with comforting remedies until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is kept closed by the eyelid on both sides of a circle of fabric until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a serious appearance, pierce it gently with a thin stylet that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor come out and let the eyelid droop and enter inward; then extract it until it heals.
de la bowe de l’oil	Here's the corrected translation:
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a swelling that forms on the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you should have the patient sit on an appropriate and straight chair, then hold their head with both hands and move it until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then let it be pierced and do not let the light escape and let the patient see things as they used to. And if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin stylet and insert it through the cornea in a hole along the conjunctiva with the cornea and the cornea, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or boiled water with fenugreek and honey, then cure it with another remedy until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similar fluids in the division, and what is required to pierce (them); and we work according to the health (of the patient). It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper for the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the size of a radish in that flesh of the eye at the part of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces the flesh of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary for the measure of the way of the almagda to be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the darkness (of the eye); and this is the crown of the eye; and you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horned veil, and then put the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it down one way after another. If the water comes out now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After resting for a little while, and if the water rises again along the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and does not rise any more, then gently remove the almagda by turning your hand back and forth; and then put a little bit of gemstone salt into the eye, and raise the eye inside. Then put cotton or wet wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk on top of it, and bind it with the healthy eye. We (and those of our time) place upon it common bread soaked with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for some men have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then only pierce the ligament, and do not go too deep, but make a shallow incision, then put on a styptic as we have said; and at the completion of the task, prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping aid, in which they sleep on their back in a dark room; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and have him look at some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not at all suitable for you to do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess is about to come, you shall unbind the eye before the seventh day and direct it towards what soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed down, then unbind the vision and place on his face a bandage to cover for some days, and always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house little by little, and return to your usual activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Ireland, who told us that in their country they make styptic by piercing, from which one sucks the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of styptic, because those who do not know them may see it; and they should be made of pure copper:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same delicateness, and their tails in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh above the nostrils
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes diverse fleshy growths are born on or near the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such growths that have a swollen flesh of fox color, and others have soft flesh of good color. In the case of these fleshy growths that are soft, but not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply the cautery to those growths and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp spatula on one side, until you know for certain that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with a very fine and light instrument so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood stops and all of the flesh is removed, then pour vinegar or water on the nose.[Source language: Old French]
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose opens and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that flesh has grown in the bone above, which the instrument cannot reach; then you must insert a fairly thick linen thread, with nodes not too far apart, and wet it with your own hands, and have the patient place the end of the thread in their nostril to the best of their ability, and pull it out while sniffing until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and children often do this in school, and it is an easy task for those who want to do it; then hold the part that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other part that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know which node has rotted the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment dissolves all remaining flesh; and then place a piece of wooden cane in the nose for several days until it is healed, and use drying medicines if necessary; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, such as a funnel, and the spout the same; and if you wish, make a closed funnel, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from (the) nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a sickness arises in the head of the nose that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you should cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then place the cautery or hot medicine on it; and if you wait until it has grown large before cutting it, see if it is hard, of a purple color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of purple color, and you see that you can remove it completely, then empty the patient and cut it carefully without fear, and cure the area with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then align the two lips in a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must cauterize all the parts of their edge until they heal, then align the two lips in a stitch and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or another healing plaster on top of it, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is to align the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses like peas, sometimes smaller and sometimes larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision in each nodule, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply the place after the incision with powdered vitriol until the blood stops flowing; and then leave it open to air, and cure the place of dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swollen flesh arises on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccating powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, you should cut it again and cauterize it; for it will not come back after cauterization. And these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of abscesses or swellings
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, scabs that are ugly and rough appear on the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, greenish, or gray, indicating corruption reaching the gum, causing the teeth to stink; in this case, you should make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape off the visible parts of the affected teeth and scabs until nothing remains; and similarly for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, continuing until they are clean. And if you remove what appears to be loose at first, that is good; if not, repeat the process on the second and third days until everything has been removed. Be aware that teeth require various shapes of instruments for scraping depending on the work required, as the scrapers used between the teeth have different forms from those used for the front surfaces of the teeth; and be sure to have all necessary forms prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache, you should delay drilling as much as possible, for it is not something to be done hastily, as the substance of the tooth is very valuable until there is no other option for relieving pain.[REGENERATIVE MEDICINE: AN OVERVIEW](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2676341/)Regenerative medicine is a branch of translational research in tissue engineering and molecular biology which deals with the process of replacing, engineering or regenerating human cells, tissues or organs to restore or establish normal function. This field holds the promise of regenerating damaged tissues and organs in the body by replacing damaged tissue or lost cells due to disease, injury or congenital defects. This field is closely related to tissue engineering and molecular biology as well as stem cell research.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is ready to pull, you should make sure of the decayed tooth. Often it happens that pain deceives the patient, and they think it is a healthy tooth, and have a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, for the abscess remains, as we have often seen with surgeons; and when you are certain of the decayed tooth, you should cauterize around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum from all sides; then pull it with your fingers or delicate pliers, gently at first and then more firmly, until it is well extracted, then fasten the pliers well; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on each side, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is decayed and hollow, you must fill it with cloth, where the holes are; and pull it delicately with pliers, so that it does not break while pulling; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part in, causing greater pain for the patient due to the malice of the root. Be careful not to act as some ignorant surgeons do, who hastily and with arrogance sometimes break the jaw, without bringing any relief as we have mentioned; but instead cause great harm due to the roots left behind or the broken jaw, as we have often seen; and once the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, or salt water; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply a little vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize the area.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to pull teeth first should have long and thick handles that do not bend when pulling the tooth. Here are the forms (shapes):
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick size so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be made of good iron, and let them have teeth to hold on to wounds.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling, you should place cotton wet with butter on the spot for one or two days until the area is softened, then use tongs called "algefri", which resemble a surgeon's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all those tongs, you must cut open the flesh all around the root, and place in it the instrument called "althali", that is, a scalpel, of this shape:[Notes](Note: The above translations are based on my best interpretation of the Old French text provided. I am not a professional translator, so there may be some errors or nuances that I have missed. Additionally, medical terminology in the 12th-13th centuries is quite different from modern medical terminology, so some terms may be difficult to translate accurately.)
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break easily, and if the root jumps out with this, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, whose shapes are shown below:[Notes](Note: The above translations are based on my best interpretation of the Old French text provided. I am not a professional translator, so there may be some errors or nuances that I have missed. Additionally, medical terminology in the 12th-13th centuries is quite different from modern medical terminology, so some terms may be difficult to translate accurately.)
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this tool which has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these tools be strong enough that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and likewise other tools which are not mentioned here; and the wise master subtly finds his own tool according to what his work and the illness reveals, because there are such diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity; and one breaks neither the cartilage nor other bones, or it will rot, so one searches among the tools that are needed, as I have said, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
