Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy enough to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but rather holds and removes it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this purpose, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, use this entire tool to scrape it away:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is not erupted after it should have, and it is not in the correct position, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it down; but if it is protruding over the other tooth, take this instrument with the shape shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron, and...
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And place the muzzle on the mouth and keep it there for several days due to the tooth's hardness, so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file such as this one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the file used to make needles; and file down the tooth lightly for several days so that it does not move until it heals; then use a flat instrument at the end, similar to a razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth come in or grow in. The word "lochent" is the present tense of the verb "locher", which means to come out, sprout, or break through (as in the case of teeth). So, "quant li dent lochent" can be translated as:
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be constricted with a golden thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and place it doubled between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth on top of the thread, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering it up to the point where you started, and gently but firmly pull on the thread until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the loose teeth with pliers and align them, placing them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, so that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the thread breaks, constrict it again with another thread; if it stays and serves in this way for its entire time, and this is the method for aligning two healthy teeth and two loose teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled meddle with it; and sometimes the shape of a bone from an animal is made, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is a tie under the tongue that is natural and present at birth, or it can occur due to an accidental closing of a wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your hands, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous band that holds it in place with a large enough incision so that the tongue is loosened from its support. And if there is toughness or knots, which comes from sudden wound closing, use a hook to cut this connective tissue. Be careful not to make the incision too deep, as the artery is located beneath it. Once you have done this, rinse the area with rose water and/or warm or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue. The patient should use it every night to prevent reconnection. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder to the wound, and if the bleeding persists, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose. Then continue treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then throw the "oncine" (a type of medical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, then apply vinegar powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the limb easily and gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come within the throat growths that are called "godath," and they are properly referred to as "the two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be cautious: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and bluish-black color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, then do not touch it at all with iron, for fear of causing bleeding; but leave it until it has matured, and only then will you divide it, or it will break open by itself; and if it is of whitish color and the root is fine, then prepare the instrument to cover (the abscess), but first see whether the hard swelling is at rest and calm. Then have the patient sit with his chin facing the sun, and let his head be in your lap, and the servant hold open his mouth and take the instrument with both hands, and press down the tongue beneath the entire instrument, of which this is the method; and it should be made of fine silver or copper as thin as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you press the tongue down with this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the "oncine" (a type of medical instrument) and stick it in the almond (swollen lymph node), and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, of which this is the method, that resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have closed one of the almonds (lobes of the tonsils), close the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's throat with warm water, or water and vinegar, and if there is bleeding, rinse the patient's throat with water, or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses form in the throat besides the two almonds (lobes of the tonsils), so cut them out in the same way as the two almonds (lobes of the tonsils).
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I treated a woman for an abscess in her throat, which was quite large and obstructing her windpipe, such that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked and could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for one day or two. And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two teeth out of her nostrils. I hurried then and inserted a probe into one of the nostrils, extracted pus, and drained a lot of matter; then I did the same in the other nostril and opened her mouth while pressing on her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut out some of it, and only a little blood came out; and so, the blocked passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut the abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing and filling up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; so I performed surgery on it and cauterized it inside her throat: this stopped its growth, and I left. And I do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye (eye-related)
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, this is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye". Once it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is thin, then it is necessary to make an incision; and this one that is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of a fuse color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision on it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the needle into the eye, and pull it downwards, and make an incision with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut further than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a ruse with cauterization without fear. And the manner of the cautery is sharp pointed. And this is that the patient places their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and apply live hot water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the movement of this instrument, whose form is as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be a hair or something to hold the medicine, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument on top of all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie down on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause choking. Then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for a quarter of an hour, until you see it reddened and the bites of the medicine are calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the wound above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is finished, then let it dry, and it will fall off after 3 or 5 days. And if you need to restart the cauterization of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery, wrap the area around the eye with cotton stuffed with butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take hyssop and rosemary and oregano and rue and chamomile and elderberry and similar herbs, and mix them all together in one pot, and add water, and bring to a boil. And let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the pieces be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye is mortified; then rinse it often, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it unless the abscess has cooled down. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to irritate the mouth, and this is a good remedy together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often, a bone or fish spine, or any other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what is not visible to you and has lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit, when the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of cloth, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of reed in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter the throat more easily and keep the head raised up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis or choke the patient, nor push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient inserts the instrument themselves, so they can feel where the object is located; whether they push it down, or pull it out completely with the instrument, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the veins are treated, as I have said in the division, with medical cures; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the vein, then pull it with a tiny hook, or with delicate pliers worth for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a bladder, and put it in the sick person's throat, then put a hot iron on the bladder's movement. And do this often. And if the patient becomes feverish all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a pierced cloth, and in this hole place the opening of the instrument; then put your fumigation in, and the patient puts the end of the bladder in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the vein; and the vein will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one pulls the vein, it is, when it can be seen, similar to bent pliers so as to easily enter the throat; and resembles a surgeon's beak, and has roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what memory brings forth hereafter, one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture. And the second manner is according to their locations in the body. For the abscess of the head is different than that of the base, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different than that which comes in joints, and each one has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is completely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have become corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the base, so one should pierce it when it is dead; and one must not pierce a grown abscess without completion of digestion, except for that which is near the base, lest it rot inwardly and become elongated, forming a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the place where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and at nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And in those that crease, according to the member. And when abscess is in fleshy parts, it is better to leave the incision until it has strengthened after completion of digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body's fluid will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and the depths become hardened. And there are some abscesses that must be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what is necessary for the member. And one must enlarge in small abscesses with small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses that require cutting out the core and covering it; when it has become as one cloth and is dead, it must be done as with boils: and there are some that are cut in three angles, and some that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of glands; and some that require a round cut, and other cuts and similar cutting out.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no visible swelling, such as a soft abscess, you should fully pierce; and when the abscess is large, and has collected pus, you should not pull out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this many times, gradually, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak vitality, such as women, small children, old and frail men. For the spirit sometimes jumps at the moment of pus expulsion, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not notice. Therefore, be very cautious in this matter, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a clean cut, then apply linen or old cotton bandages; but if it is large abscesses with many holes, then you should put in a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and turned it over, then you should fill it with old linen rags or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and dress the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and a wet cloth to the area multiple times. If the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is during winter, and the place where the abscess is located is very sensitive, then you should put tents and wet cloths soaked in warm wine and oil on it; and if it is in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and wipe it and dress it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	The word "des soros" in Old French refers to swellings or tumors. It can be translated into English as "abscesses" or "swellings". In modern medical terminology, it could refer to a variety of conditions such as cysts, boils, abscesses, or other soft tissue masses.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where boils of the head come forth as small abscesses, and they are of various kinds that are in skins, such as the joints of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture, like those of poultry; and there are others that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. And the work of cutting is such that you test with every single instrument called an "entromissoire", the form of which comes after, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, you pierce it from above along the long side. And when the moisture has been emptied, you skin without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again when anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain from the night will clean it. And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are certain that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound with an appropriate ointment, until it is healed. And if the abscess holds a hard knot, you cut it along the long side; and you throw your leeches there, and skin it all around, and put all your effort into drawing out the cyst that lies there; and if the artery opposes you, do what I told you after. And similarly for the abscess if it is stony, and to cut and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting into hard and moist abscesses is easier, for they contain little blood. And some of these abscesses, on the head or where there is no moisture, and this was one of the abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard and rough and white as a stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it with any object, they would have made as much of a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except those that come on children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that pus may easily exit; and cure them as is proper.
des scrophules	The term "scrophules" refers to a type of abscess or swollen lymph node, typically found in the neck. The name comes from the Greek word "skirphere", meaning "hard tubercle". Scrofula is often associated with tuberculosis infection and was commonly referred to as the "King's Evil" in medieval Europe, where it was believed that the touch of a monarch could cure the disease. However, this belief has been proven to be false and scrofula is now treated with antibiotics and other medical interventions.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	"Scrophules" often appear in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes occur elsewhere on the body, and are multiple, adhering to one another. Each scrofula is specifically located in its own cavity, like a knot or head abscess as we have said; and there are many similarities between these scrophules. Some contain moisture, and some are malignant and do not want to submit to health. In that case, where you see it in good condition to touch, and is the color of the skin, and moves on every side and does not adhere to the nerves of the neck or artery or duct, and is not deep; then it should be cut open from above, and the skin removed from all sides, and the two lips of the wound stretched apart with leeches if necessary, as we have said in head abscesses; and draw out little by little, being careful not to cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp or cutting, lest the hands slip and it cuts too deep, removing what should not be removed.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop blood and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skill if there remain any small scrofulous parts, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not appropriate to cut that scrofula at its root, but bind it with a double strong thread, and let it fall without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut all of the scrofula, it is necessary to bring together the two edges of the wound and sew it now, as there is no longer any excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary to focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said. For those scrofulas that have an excess, pierce where it appears dead; and pierce it as we previously mentioned, letting it hang, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption. And when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a healing ointment until the flesh becomes healthy.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" in Old French can be translated to "of sciatica" in English. Sciatica is a condition that causes pain in the lower back and hips, often due to pressure on the sciatic nerve.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke and wrote about the operation of the throat (i.e. tracheotomy), but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it; it is only written in their texts.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the divider of the throat called "epiglote" be loosened; and this is not done with the help of anyone, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are closed to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two amandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to divide the epiglote, it is necessary that we divide it under three or four circles, a small slit of the crosswise, between the two circles or according to the size of the fissure of the syphilis, not in the cartilage.[ ](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/cartillaige#fr)
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these locations are suitable for the division of the epiglote where there is no flesh, and the veins are long and narrow.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the windpipe; and release the vessels of blood, if you see any such thing, and then cut the syringe, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that jumps out through the broken opening, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.[2](#footnote2 'Note 2')
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the throat and sew it up all the way to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it has healed completely.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cauterize the epiglottis to prevent the patient from swallowing, and they will breathe through the wound, and in this way, they are kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the danger of the disease has passed, and this takes three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they ordered to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the tendons in the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had flowed from it, and I knew for certain that she had not opened a vein or directed it away from her throat, and the wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cured it until it healed;[INTUIT: The text uses a word "sanee" which is not present in my dictionary. However, given the context, I assume that it means "healed".]
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And nothing more happened to the damsel than that her voice became hoarse, and she later returned to normal.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore, I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a lentil, and it is common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is of two kinds: natural and accidental; the natural one has no intelligence.[---]
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental type is also of two kinds: one resembles fatty tissue, and the other kind resembles an abscess that arises from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and one should not dare to make an incision that is large, but rather try and probe with the whole instrument:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a hard knot and it cannot be opened by any vein, then cut it, just as one would cut a knot, and pull it out completely with its covering, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search thoroughly and treat it as necessary until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	of the knots or nodes. The word "nous" in Old French can refer to a knot or node, and is sometimes used in medical texts to describe hardened lumps or swellings in the body. In this context, it may be referring to an abnormal growth or swelling in the body that needs to be treated.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways (kinds) are there, which I will tell you all the likenesses (similarities);
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary that I tell you all the differences that are between nouwt (dislocation) and issue (discharge).
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is heat and fever holding, until the ebullition (boiling) has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a dislocation there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one abscess (infection), which is its own sac and according to the color of the body, and begins like a pustule, and becomes large;[
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And there are two similarities, either fatty or moist, and they are very diverse in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and inquire about the instrument called "entromissoire," according to its form as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way to inquire about abscesses of the nose is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess and turn your fingers back and forth until you know that the instrument has penetrated the core, then according to the size of the abscess.[ ](https://www.duolingo.com/comment/36958017$comments)
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the entromissoire and take care that nothing falls out.[ ](https://www.duolingo.com/comment/36958017$comments)
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs out of it and it has the same color as I have said about other abscesses, let it flow.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision, moisture does not come, know that it is fatty, then make a cross shape and take tongs, and lightly skin it from each side and pull the coat [or covering] where it lies healthy with the new [growth];
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out whole, then tear it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pain will come back many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if some remains and it troubles you, then apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind it up, and apply soothing hot compresses to promote healing, treating other wounds until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, then suture the two lips of the wound and treat it until the flesh is healed.[Note: "enjanre" means to injure or harm]
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the swollen veins are contrary to you or otherwise, hurry and use the vitriol powder, and leave it there for two or three days, until the wound dries out, and let the boiling of the blood subside; then return to cover what remains of the new [incision].
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of the inserted instruments, which are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to enclose abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are similar to the needles used to sew surplices, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and are proven to be better for enclosing the hollow spaces of a fistula.[*I translated "corbeures" as "hollow spaces", because I think it refers to the inner part of the fistula, which is hollow, but I'm not 100% sure.*]
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the kidneys are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are kidneys that have two bumps of three kinds as well;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And there are kidneys that have three bumps, and they are also of three kinds; and there are kidneys that have two bumps, and others that have only one bump, and they too are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these (kidneys) are sharp, and some only cut on one side, so that we flay the flesh to avoid cutting the vein or nerve.[Car l'un des costez est couvert d’une grant membraine qui a la char engloee dedens, et por ceu est il mauvais a traire.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these intestines are folded back in folds, so that the patient does not notice their removal during the incision of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and they are not used anywhere except on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and ankles, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes, they make another small instrument, resembling the scabs of abscesses, in this shape, to stop bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And they sometimes place it on the wound that bleeds profusely from veins and arteries, and sometimes with this larger shape:[![image](1602978539457.png)](https://i.stack.imgur.com/cCfjr.png)
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupt, so much that they resemble women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	"And they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must act according to the form of this line b, up to g."
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"Then, remove the fat and apply medicine to the wound with inflaming flesh, then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches and continue to care for it until it is healed."
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	"And if the breasts sag downward and are soft due to their size, as it often happens with women, then make two cuts on top of them in a similar manner."[Note: This passage seems to be describing some kind of surgical procedure for correcting sagging or enlarged breasts.]
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	"So that one is held to the other at the end of each, in such a way that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from the line b up to the line g." et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient will not rest, or due to blood loss, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive salve;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it in place until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then continue to treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulous sores or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Then those who contain moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with aged cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply appropriate ointment to it until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulas, treat it as we have said for scrofulous sores, and if the wound becomes pussy again, apply a cauterization as we have mentioned before.[Translate]
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin on top is closed, it often results in abscesses, and the same thing happens when a vein becomes swollen and develops an abscess.[Translate]
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and one knows it thus when it is because of the artery, so the abscess is long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, it feels like a tightness; and when it is because of the vein, it is swollen and clearly visible;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And it is foolish to cover this abscess, and even when it is beneath the nails, or under the armpits and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.[
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid iron treatment and also the one who is at the head should avoid it as well, and in case of swelling of the artery, make an incision through the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make an incision along the groin, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle beneath it, and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then place the instrument between the two ties and press it until blood comes out, thus releasing the abscess;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then treat the wound to help it heal well, until the ties fall off by themselves.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply appropriate ointments to the wound, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is because of the opening of the vein, then you should touch with your hand as much of the abscess as possible.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then insert the needle under the area you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce through, and have a double thread so that you can pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with one of the two ends of the double thread around the two edges of the wound.[p. 3]
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you fear that the thread might come out, insert another needle through the entire length of the thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle and tighten the threads in four places.[p. 3][ST1][ENDFOOTNOTE]
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess as much as necessary for the pus to come out, then cut off the excess skin and leave what has been bound.[p. 3][ST1][ENDFOOTNOTE][ST2][ENDFOOTNOTE]
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then provide treatments of tents and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can come in the artery and vein, an abscess comes to the nerves when they are wounded or by excessive exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulders and arms and in all places where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the skin, and it is in various forms without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is strongly constricted, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but beneath the chest;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it moves well in all directions, but goes neither forward nor backward, nor downward or upward, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is on the head or forehead, makes the skin suppurate.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it with a string and flay it, then remove it and bring the wound together with sutures, and treat it until it heals.[INTUITIVE: The text appears to be describing a medical procedure for treating abscesses, either by cutting them at their root if they are small or removing them and stitching up the wound if they are large.
