It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the figure of natural childbirth and its signs, which are when you see the woman pressing downwards and desiring to smell the air; then the child hastens to come out; therefore, know that this birth is according to nature, and the exit is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, then gently press on her stomach so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the groin is cleansed of its impurities by good cleansing; and any birth that comes differently does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes with its feet first, or outside the body or the legs, or the hands, or it comes on its stomach, or turns over onto its neck, or in other bad figures; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these things, and to be wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures and how one should help in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of the womb headfirst, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a chair or have women hold her; and anoint her vagina with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then insert for her the small speculum of the following form:

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon to treat the wound, and I thought for a long time, but could not heal the wound.

et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she gives birth as a result of this, it is good.

toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over the fire; then place a lid or stopper on the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marshes patient.

et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if it does not come out despite all that we have said, be careful not to pull too hard.

Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is appropriate to use suitable fumigations for this: some of the ancients have tried fumigation of watercress and dried figs.

Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is made of glass, similar to a small tube, and the narrow end is placed in the vagina, while the wide ends are suspended over the fire;

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the bottom / to puncture the fundus (as in childbirth)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have their bottom pierced, but rather it is stopped up by a subtle membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane correctly with her finger, and not prick it with a small knife, and ensure she does not touch the instrument (used in childbirth).
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place wet wool soaked in wine and oil on it, then cure it with a salve until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you are worried that it might become blocked again, place a piece of wood in the opening and leave it for several days, removing it when the child wants to go to the chamber pot (to defecate).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes, these stoppages happen as a result of sudden closure of a wound or abscess; such a closure needs to be covered and treated, as we have said with the willow splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the anus are hard and grow near the anus or in the space of the two parts (buttocks).
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one fistula or multiple, and when this hardening is old, it works (the fistula opens), and furthermore moisture appears, which is white pus or thin serous fluid.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is a discharge or flatulence when the patient passes stool, and perhaps even in the form of worms.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the groin.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus, one knows a fistula reaching to the anus, and not penetrating it.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And this is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and then carefully introducing a fine needle of steel or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity (twisting).
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity (twisting), then insert a slender probe made of reed or a horsehair until you feel it with your finger;[INTO THE FIStula]
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it (the probe/hair) and it does not come out of the opening, nor is there any sign of evacuation of waste or gas, as we have said;[INTO THE FIStula][INTO THE Finger in the fistula (as sensing agent)]
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce deeply; so hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches down to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, if urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it (the fistula) is pierced down to the joint of the thigh, then the vein extends down to that place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the source of pain is not around it, then it (the limb) will be bent from now on, and neither medicine nor healing through ointment will help.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these pierced fistulas, there is no cure except for labor and the foolishness of so-called physicians who meddle with it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In the one who is not pierced and not old, there is hope of health through iron, as I have tested.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And it is necessary for the patient to lie in your hands on their back, with legs raised up to their thighs, and have their thighs bent towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then insert a tent of iron or wood if there is curvature, so that you know where the tent comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it near their anus, then you must insert your little finger there.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if you then feel that the tendon has pierced it; and is exposed where you feel between your thumb and index finger, know that it is severed;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is true that some can be healed, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that one can provide is to heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caut%C3%A8re\_subtil](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caut%C3%A8re_subtil)

et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat inflamed tents with butter, until the flesh comes out, then treat them with a spreading ointment that heals and binds wounds.

et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the abscess enters (the body) but does not reach the finger that is at its base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue between your finger and the abscess, and you see the fistula follow the thick covering of the skin;

Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood rushes at you and flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or a medicinal agent.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of the affected parts and the stopping of blood and drying up of moisture.

puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat wounds with boiling, running substances that harden the flesh, and use dry medicines.

Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the deep bottom, and is separated from the body, place your finger in the bottom and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the swelling and between two is the tissue or the abscess or flesh, or it is about to break open, then there is no other option but to have faith and hope in one of the three following methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it open to the bottom, or if possible, you apply bandages and treat it as in the first instance.

Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted thread through it (the hole) into both (ends), and push the tent peg fully into the fistula up to the head.

It looks like a spindle with a pointed end and a blunt end.](https://i.imgur.com/gallery/6hLGwvT.png)
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and some are outside the anus and at the opening of the anus; but those that are outside cause little moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	And still sometimes there is a little yellow water or a little blood, and they have the color of the flesh;[IT] Et quant il sont en telle maniere, si ne sont mie bien;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to strain when going to the bathroom so that the anus protrudes and the veins can be seen.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you rush and pierce it with pincers, or hold it with your nail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the hooks cannot hold it due to its moisture, then take a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of cameline;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	And pull them out with your hands, then cut it and sprinkle some hot powders on it as a substitute for cautery;[**]
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or cauterize it as described in the chapter on cautery, then cure it with other cures until it is healed;[**][^1]
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the foundation cannot come out, then administer an aggressive and bitter enema to the patient to clean what is in the rectum so that it may come out openly;[**][^1]
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient can move, and if the threads are out of place, then the treatment is easy.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you should take them with your nail or with pincers, and cut them, then treat it as we have said until it is healed, and make sure the patient fears incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	You should prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread beneath the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and make it of appropriate width; pull the thread tight, then knot the thread and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one to tie off any excess blood
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place a cloth soaked in oil of roses or cerote on the wound, and place it on the foundation, and tell the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it (the part) be until it has set, and when it has fallen off, cure it with a salve and other cures, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dry pus or feces
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is dry pus in the intestines, due to constipation of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not helpful.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	One should scrape with the tip of a spatula or your nail the crust on top so it doesn't moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure (it) until it is dry as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then shave it again more forcefully than before, until it heals well, and let it be scarified;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	trembling/shivering[START OF THE NEXT SENTENCE] Li malaides se desconforte, si li convient porter chauze et panoz;
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica (the term used here for "formica" is not the same as the modern word for ants) is a small hole that appears in the body and goes very deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes it is found to be knotted (frois), and its presence can be felt like a tremor of death throughout the body, particularly in the hands.[START OF THE NEXT SENTENCE] Et cestui mal se puet faire par maintes choses;
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a reed from a goose feather, or a strong swan feather, and place that reed on the spine, so that the circle covers the entire spine;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand along the entire reed so that you touch all around the spine, and push it in deep, and pull the spine from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a reed of bronze or iron in the same manner, being fine underneath and trailing above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not puncturing, so as to hold it with the finger, and pressing gently. And if you wish, cauterize the spine, as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of an enema.[](Note: I'm assuming that the previous sentence was "Cauterize the spine with a red-hot iron rod, as we have previously described in the chapter on cautery." And the current sentence is a continuation of the previous one, indicating that the shape of the instrument to be used for cauterization should be similar to an enema.)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes, a enema is made of silver or brass, or melted tin or lead; and sometimes it is made with various sized instruments, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then those who are prepared for the care of children and who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large enema is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the intestines perforated; and on one side there should be two openings, and on the other, one.[img](https://i.imgur.com/Z0CvRfN.png)
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly (enema bag) in which one places the medicine is made from an animal bladder or parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have one finger's width between each hole, then insert into these holes a strong thread twisted in ten or twelve strands, and bind the belly like a goat's saddle girth.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform an enema; and this is the method of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the end of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or a similar substance, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister presses it with both hands until it is all expelled, then removes the enema and lifts the patient's legs in the air.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the medicine wants to come out, let it do so as much as it can; and if they sleep through the night, it will be more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine rushes out, then reinserts it until it is stable.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the anus or abscessed, then let the enema be as thin as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of a thin enema, with the skin stretched tight:[ lí forme dou clistere subtil = the form/shape of the thin enema]
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division about the care of wounds; now we will tell you about the care of hands and of remedies, according to their implementation.[nos = we (plural)]
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are: by striking with a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or with a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or according to the parts of the body where wounds are located, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure for each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head, for reminders will come in their own chapter
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, pay attention if it is from striking with a stone or similar things, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you should lightly incise for a hot abscess: do it immediately with the cephalic itself if it comes with little blood from the wound, and let the incision be opposite the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and let the patient abstain from wine and heavy meals.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to be incised, let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is entirely fresh with all its blood and not exposed to air, powder, which I will mention a little later.[IST] Et se il vient y aposteme chaut, si ne li soit mis nul autre chose devant que la dictée pouldre;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeons have moved it, put some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword and similar ones, and the lips cannot come together with sutures, then bring them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds of the abdomen, through stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and hangs, and only holds on by a little, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and roasted wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.[CODAI] Here is a possible translation of the entire passage:
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten flesh in the skin, and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all the decayed flesh and throw it out, then cure (the wound).
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without a coat, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, you must tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: and that is to apply this powder which coagulates once the wound has been cleaned.[Read More](https://hellotext.com/blog/medieval-french-text-translation/)
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	The method for making the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts quicklime, and grind it into a fine powder.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly so that it dries out completely and is fully absorbed into the blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with cauterizing irons only, when incense or dragon's blood is not available, but as long as the surgeon has not yet moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the surgeon has already touched the wound, one does not apply this powder at all.[Reference(s):
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but instead applies digestive ointments or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey until it discharges pus.[Reference(s):
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then one treats it with other treatments until it is healed.[Reference(s):
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of bones comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except when a nerve or artery of the neck is cut.[INTOXICATED = under the influence of poison; INTOXICATION = the condition of being intoxicated]
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound open and not apply any constricting agent, because it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, such as chalk washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and also lily washed in clean water,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of this kind, prepared in the same way, and moist ointments.[Comment: "pieres de mine" means "stones with medicinal properties"]
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.[Comment: "cout" means to sew or stitch; "bendes" means bandages or strips of cloth]
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and have festered, swollen and filled with pus, then lance it or incise it at a lower place;[Comment: "parfondes" means deep; "chevee" means swollen; "pleinne de bowe" means filled with pus
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if an artery is cut, and there is a flow of blood, then tie it off, and bind it up, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and it is kept intact so that food can pass through.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	Then place the windpipe on the groove of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then bind it appropriately, and leave it for several days, and then cure it with discarded onion treatments until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then cure it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave them until the wound festers.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let the dislocation be released and realigned.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder that I have mentioned on it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is also a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.[NOTE: The word "fistula" here refers to an abnormal duct or passage within the body, often between two internal organs or leading from an internal organ to the skin's surface. It can be caused by injury, infection, or disease.]
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound caused by a spear or knife.[NOTE: These two objects are mentioned specifically as examples of sharp weapons that can cause deep and potentially infected wounds.]
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a strike from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if any breeze blows out of the wound when the patient exhales; then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at once or bind it tightly in the first hour, for fear that the blood may not flow properly.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And return the blood to the heart and quickly treat the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	But apply an attractive ointment and bind it two times per day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	And if you do not have any ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture.  [(Note: I'm assuming "viel" means "old" or "used," and "succier" is a misspelling of "secher," which means "dry")]
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	there will be no spasm, nor bad tremors of the heart or twitchings of the sinew;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with bandages and other treatments, until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and pus forms, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is straightforward, or worse on the side or back, then treat the one in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, suture it; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is close to the bone, and has broken off pieces, then clean the wound, and pull out any loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not loose, then let the wound rot, it will make extraction easier.[*](Note: This may seem like a barbaric treatment but in medieval medicine, letting wounds suppurate and rot was a common practice to avoid infection.)
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And the judgement for other wounds on different limbs is as we have said. (This implies that the same principles and treatments discussed earlier in the text should be applied to wounds on various parts of the body.)[*](Note: This sentence assumes the reader has prior knowledge of the text's guidelines for treating wounds. This highlights how medieval medical texts often relied on established doctrines, assuming the reader had access to the same educational background as the author.)
dou derrompement dou ventre	
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	In a large wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, causing their entry (into the wound);[*](note: I'm assuming "intromission" here means the protrusion of intestines or nerves into the wound)
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	And the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one,[*](note: I'm assuming "li petit plaie" refers to "small wound" here)
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Therefore, one delays in returning the intestines with pins if they are not returned immediately while still warm (with body temperature);[*](note: I'm assuming "poinnes" here refers to pins or needles used for suturing)
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, and they contract more when pricked,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and therefore it is better to make a minor wound, so that one can reset the intestines to their proper place more easily than with the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that there are four types of ruptures in the abdomen:

The reason is that "plonc" in Old French specifically refers to a type of metal that is heavy and malleable, similar to lead. This means that the probe made of this material can bend easily around the twists and turns of the fistula, allowing for more accurate probing. I wanted to point this out because it's an interesting aspect of medieval medicine that showcases the use of specific materials for medical procedures, based on their physical properties. Please let me know if you have any questions or concerns.][
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot fully surround it with probes,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then irrigate it through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For moisture easily travels from one hole to another and cleanses it,
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then attempt to cause bleeding according to your ability, so that you can determine if there is bone or nerve inside, and whether it goes deep within.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressing with your hand, and the location where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein,

puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	Then place dampened tents (medical bandages) in medicine, and insert them up to the top of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine consumes the excess matter that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then apply heated poultices of clean flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	And if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize it as we have previously mentioned.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not trouble you in the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, scrape it until all of the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with healing things on the flesh until it is healed;[ST1]
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed, and returns crooked as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not yet gone to the source;
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	uncover and search until you reach the bottom.

et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is then healed in this way, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	unless otherwise, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	except for leaving it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small fractured bone, and you can pull it out with tongs,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you extract it with a suitable instrument for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, pull all of them out and do not leave even one.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	And if moisture causes opposition, without any mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if the bone is covered by flesh and moisture, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something putrefactive on the wound,

et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will come out more easily;

Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to something that entered his body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matter reached the leg and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no apparent reason to open it;[

et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared through which all sorts of impurities and moisture from the body exited.

Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	"I pitched a tent in one of these veins, and then searched all the veins,"[Note: This is a metaphorical use of the word "veins". je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I thought what appeared to me of the rotten bone was all there was, except for that which I removed.[INT-1: ] et demoura puis une piece de char toute nue, si grant come ung denier, de quoi li veins estoit tous dessechez.

Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a ligament, and tie it to the end of the broken bone that is visible,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct someone to stretch it out high;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another larger linen ligament, and tie it to the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you draw out the rotten flesh underneath,

et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupt joint and bind the bone that contains it on the other side;[IST) Et se tu voels departir li tisons, si soit il brief et net, sans chaundelier.

dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head (of an abscess) rots either from within or from without;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have treated this corruption with the help of medicines, but they do not help at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then the member should be covered until the place where the corruption has reached;
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes from death by this, or from the greater evil, which is the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the sign of this is that the limb becomes black, as if it has been burned by fire.

et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they (the incisions) do not reach the bone or the nerve, and such a condition is called "wasting disease."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it (the abscess) becomes so long that it reaches the bone deep inside, it is then called "fistula".[INTRODUCTION]: This text is from a medieval medical treatise written in Old French during the 12th-13th centuries. It describes various surgical procedures and conditions, including cauterization, dislocations, wounds, abscesses, and wasting disease. The author advises patients to let their hair grow long for fire cautery treatment, while avoiding shaving at the base of the affected area. They also describe a procedure for treating shoulder dislocations due to moisture by resetting the joint and waiting for it to heal without movement. Additionally, they differentiate between wasting disease and fistula, specifying that an abscess reaching the bone is considered a fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the leather is such that you cut all around it, and similarly when it is fine, like a piece of cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And do not be afraid to cut it, due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you are concerned that the leather will harden, and the corruption is not deep,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if the leather is thick with flesh, then cure it with an enema in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look and see if the blisters are large, and if the boil which is in it has a foul smell,[INTSANT] si le clistre eschauffe de fenugrec ou de serapion blanc, et se tu veus que il soit plus chaut, met y de poivre.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then perform an enema of Egyptian medicine, which is made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloes, oil, and litharge in equal amounts, and cook them together in a vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take as much of this as you need, dilute it in water and honey,[ST1]{\*}{\*}
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and use it to perform an enema on the patient while constricting the anus.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for 2 hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is emptied and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at times, perform an enema with ashes water,[OED, s.v. clisterise, v.\]: "To give (a person) an enema; to irrigate or cleanse the bowels of (a person) by means of an enema."
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and if you take vine wood ashes and pour water over it,[OED, s.v. cinders, n.]: "(Originally in plural) The residue left after combustion; burnt coal, coke, dross, or ashes."
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then filter it, and perform an enema with it until you are certain that the breast is fully cleansed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	And if the patient cannot endure it, nor Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	give them an enema of water and honey with a bit of pulverized litharge (lead oxide);
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or give them an enema of honey and mixed wine, in which the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine causes the flesh to become soft;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are confident that the wound is well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then use an enema to promote the growth of flesh in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take a diaphoretic emplaster, made with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or use some medicines and poultices, the properties of which I have mentioned in the section on poultices.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	And if the wound in the breast is small, and the nozzle of the enema cannot enter it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you widen the wound slightly with a iron instrument, and place inside it a tent made of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or apply a basilicon ointment until it is wide enough;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then you should stitch it up so that only a space of one finger's width or enough for an enema to enter remains.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the perforation that spews pus is above, then you should place the incision or a little lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is fully drawn, no flesh is allowed to protrude.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound as you would like,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	Prepare it in such a way that the bowstring rests at the lowest point possible.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is fully drawn, no flesh should protrude.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound as you would like,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	equipped in such a manner: that the bow (or arrow) slides down easily, and leaves nothing of the bow (or arrow) behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to apply to the wound.
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and place a linen cloth over it that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then apply cautery force to the wound of the breast, one hand-span larger than the first (one).[References: a hand-span is three inches or 7.62 cm]
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the wound.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the opening of the chest to ease the swelling, and do not remove the large bandage until after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And the one who is (placed) on the chest opening, often removes (it) to reduce the swelling.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And know that it comes from the swelling, whether it is venom or pus or enough (of it), or if it is digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	And take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess present or not.[INTUITO: "aposteme" is an old French term for an abscess or collection of pus in a localized area.]
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature (the condition or symptom) arise on the chest opening,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	know that the breast has already swelled and approached the saintness;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then unbind it in the morning or in three days, and when you unbind the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change one other bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast hangs loose and bloated after many days, know that the breast has not swelled at all.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons come later after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the holy ones approach. For there are men for whom healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the contrary;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the breast becomes bloated and indigestible after many days, know that the breast is not healing;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is far from being healed, use drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and is the last medicine;[NOTE: Vitriol here likely refers to sulfates or sulfuric acid.]
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphoretic ointment and make it with rose oil, and even out the consistency with old wine.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then smear and make use of it; and the same applies when honey is cooked and thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when the application of ointments is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them, and make a powder over honey that is heated over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	And then apply it with a bandage to the affected area and lay it on the chest, occasionally administering a long-lasting medicine called "aristologe".[Note: I cannot determine what "aristologe" means because it is not a recognized term in medieval French or Latin medicine. It might be a misspelling or an obscure term specific to this text.]
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the heavenly lily, which are similar to the flour of vetch and centaury[Note: I believe "lis celeste" is a misspelling or variation on "lis clair", meaning white lilies. The reference to "farine de veces et centoire" suggests that this ingredient is ground into a fine powder like flour. Centaury is a type of medicinal herb, and vetch refers to various leguminous plants with small seeds.]
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in using simples or compounds: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has set in deeply and is exerting pressure on the bone, or on the solid members, or on the ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	similar to the treatment for a fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess on the fingernail[STH-15]: Here is a possible translation:
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A panaritium is a abscess that forms under the nail of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or foot, and may possibly form in other limbs;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	And if it is neglected when it has matured, a large abscess can form,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they will run and spread so that they reach the root of the nail, and possibly destroy it entirely;[br][ ]And when this happens, it is necessary to remove the nail to treat the abscess.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And the corruption reaches the bone, causing a painful infection with a wide opening and pus-filled discharge.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	Then you must cut away with a knife all the excess flesh that remains on the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	and then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	And if the nail begins to fester and prick, and the flesh around it becomes inflamed,[INTUITION] The text is describing an infection in the area surrounding the nail. It suggests that the cautery should be used as a treatment only when the bone and nail are healthy, but if the nail has become infected and is causing pain or swelling, then the use of cautery may not be appropriate.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	You should place the rod under the nail, without touching the flesh.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and lift it up, and carefully and lightly cut the delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicine to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, cure it with poultices until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption has reached the bone, cut it out and remove it, for as long as there is decayed bone present, it cannot heal.[INST) Et puis le cure come devant di: c’est a savoir que tu li mettes oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the finger becoming corrupt, cut it off at one of its joints as stated earlier.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded or pierced and causes great pain, you must first treat the wound;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail of the thumb at an angle, cutting across the top;
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and make sure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel excessive pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, place something on it to calm (the irritation).
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the gout in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The gouts that arise in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there are places where there are bones, and sometimes there are nails,[INTERNET CRASH AND LOSS OF PREVIOUS ANSWER. RE-SUBMITTING THE SAME TEXT FOR TRANSLATION.]
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	And some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the growth is in some of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who is born with any knot in the groin does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And he who is born at the groin joint, perhaps moves;

Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: hold him with forceps.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In the one who is born at the perineum, you must first cut the circular flesh down to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone to an appropriate size, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The unions that occur at the hands can come from birth, or from healing of a wound, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.[STT: In those who have unions (fused fingers) at the hands, these can be present from birth, or due to healing of wounds, or from cauterization by fire, or similar causes. ]
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary to cut the union, so that the fingers can regain their natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two wet tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two thin wooden plates, until the place is healed, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of these [the two wooden plates] with the palm, cut away that swelling as is necessary.[Interpretation: The instruction is to remove any excess material or swelling that may have formed between the two wooden plates while they are in place.]
