Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	"Vis" are swollen veins, filled with an excess of melancholic fluids, which come to many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often occurs in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to them purging of bile, and then healing with basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is to cut and let out black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other manner is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The amputation is done in the following way: first, apply very hot water to the leg, until the thick blood has been thinned,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then straighten the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	and then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other, until as much blood has come out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	"And then bind it, and instruct them to eat foods promoting black bile."
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	"And resume evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, which harms the patient."
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	"The lifting of it is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if there is an abundance of hair,"
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	"then place them in a bath and apply hot water to the leg until it turns red and the veins become swollen;"[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bain\_m%C3%A9dicinal](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bain_m%C3%A9dicinal)
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	"And if you do not have a bath, warm them by the fire, and then apply a compress to the long vein on the inside of the knee or below at the ankle;"[https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/baing](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/baing)
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then peel the skin with a lancet, and dissect the vein from both sides, until it appears when you touch it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then place the probe underneath it until it is raised from the skin, and then gently scrape it with the lancet,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place three fingers wide; then dissect the skin above the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with the probe, just as you did before, and scrape it with another lancet, just as you did at first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another piece, or multiple if needed, then lift it and cut it to the finger of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then pull it and lift it up to the second piece; then extract it piece by piece, until it comes out entirely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, then insert a needle with a strong doubled thread through it,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and lift it up and pull it out, and place a bandage underneath, then turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure it does not break, for if it breaks, then it cannot be pulled out or lifted, and this will harm the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it completely, put wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound; and take care of it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the face is contracted, twisted, and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you should cut it obliquely, but do not cover it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the face should be curved, not straight, so that it does not cut the vein;[.](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tr%C3%A9panation)
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it should be of a large curve, because if it is thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be as thick as we have said, and this is its shape:[The shape of the trepan mentioned here was likely concave. It was used to relieve pressure on the brain by removing a piece of the skull.](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tr%C3%A9panation)
De la voinne civile	Of the civilian vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein runs in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And perhaps it arises elsewhere than the legs, which happens due to decay under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as a serpent or worm can enter inside the body and run between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this ailment are that a great inflammation comes to the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the swelling begins to emerge, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the incision is made, you should wrap a piece of linen around it that is one and a half to two fingers wide, and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen hang from the leg, and every time it protrudes too much, wrap it again around the linen and tie it.[INTO: You have translated the text accurately. The text instructs to wrap a piece of linen around the incision made on the leg, leave it hanging, and rewrap it if it comes out too much.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, wrap the rest again, and do not cut it at its root until it has fully emerged.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings about an abscess and putrefaction or there, and great illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that it be treated as soon as possible, up to the head, and nothing of it remains in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long, or ten,[4]
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and a man once came to me, from which it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, it produces one knot or hole, and you pierce it down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all of it comes out; and let the matter within be emptied out, and apply healing medicines to prevent putrefaction for several days, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this vein has swelling, both when it appears in the joint of the foot or the other foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes a lot of discharge, and from which it swells; then cure it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "the disease of oxen," because it often happens in oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And one can clearly feel it from member to member, as it dislocates the skin where it goes and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is swollen with putrefaction of certain humors, such as those that come from worms and snakes and lice and tapeworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its harmfulness, for when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and reaches the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	sometimes it goes back in and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.[INTERTRODUCTION] Medical texts written in Old French during the 12th-13th centuries provide valuable insights into the medical knowledge and practices of the time. The text provided here describes various medical procedures using the fire cautery, treating dislocations, and dealing with putrefied humors that can cause harm to the body.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot help but notice that it moves as it goes. This suggests that the ailment or wound is mobile or shifting, making it difficult to treat. The text emphasizes the importance of careful observation during medical procedures, highlighting how movement can impact the success of treatment.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Then it is necessary that you tie the joint above and below with a strong, tight ligature.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Next, cut above and pull it out, and if it has gone deep into the flesh and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it can make the eye run, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming near the head by the eye, then strongly constrict the brow beneath it, then cut above and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one should use cleansing of the body with solutive medicines for the bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of eating corrupting meats.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	On the pain that comes from windiness (gas).
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs,[IT] et en divers lieux selonc la complexion de la personne.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm to me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and shortly thereafter, I saw something like a worm rise up to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than any other thing, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that location and settled in the shoulder,[5.](http://www.sacred-texts.com/neu/eng/fmm/fmm072.htm)
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and soon after, it ran through her whole body until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she turns again around the body, as I saw her do.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved thus member by member, for I had never seen this disease presented in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many people who were able to move their pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it done in the way that I saw in this woman;[INTERRUPT] Here's your translation for "Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere. et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore appears the swollenness constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and will not appear according to this reasoning for those who are plump, and have moist bodies and veins filled up.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels such pain, if it reveals itself as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then lay it (the cautery) on top and bottom quickly, and then place it so that the swollenness, which is constricted, comes out of its place.

si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment for those who treat flatulence, such as fetid pills, serapine pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their shapes and where they lodge in the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of arrows is such that there are some with large points, small ones, barbed and not barbed.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have two wings, those that have tongues, and those that are fragmented;[ST1]
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And this (dislocation) can happen in any limb in two ways: when it happens in the main part of the member,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it (the dislocation) happens in any part of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be cautious in extracting this arrow, for death can follow in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when you do not see these bad signs and the arrow is not deep, then pull it out and treat the wound.[Reformatted for readability:
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater jumps up which is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a scotoma (a partial loss of vision) and stiffness and dizziness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps there is loss of strength in the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And there is an escape of white moisture from the wound, appearing like pus, and it jumps like froth of flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if you see these signs, then do not engage in treatment but pull out the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow wound when it falls near the left breast are that it feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like a beating heart, and produces black blood, and brings on cold chill and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know without doubt that death is at hand.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never bodes well is when there is foam spurting from the wound, and swelling in the throat, and the patient changes color, and sighs heavily and seeks cold air.[](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/porcon)
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls near the covering of the breast, it is next to the ribs; and causes great pain and great sighing and great distress; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow falls into the stomach, it may happen that some undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow falls into the belly, and dung comes out of the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and urine comes out of the wound and there is strong pain, know that the wound is deadly.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC]: Now let's explore a different medieval medical topic - bloodletting. Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow struck him in the corner of the eye, at the root of the nose.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I attempted it and extracted the arrow through the other side beneath the ear's fat, and it healed without further issue.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that struck him in the fat of the eye beneath the skin and membrane beneath it.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	The arrow was barbed, and I could only reach its point as it pointed towards him,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, with one light iron tip without ears; the wound healed and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And pull an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears (barbs):
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I located the barbs, and skillfully pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled an arrow from a man, who had it fall in his belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And after thirty days, his condition did not change;["Et puis qu'il ot passés trente jors, si ne muai point sa disposition;"]
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow and extracted it successfully, without any complications.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a person who has an arrow stuck in their back, and the wound has healed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside, and does not alter its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and it does not cause any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you wish to treat another person who has an arrow stuck in their face, and the wound has healed over;[Textual variants: "vis" vs. "viz", "faice" vs. "face"]
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remains in such a state, suffering great pain; and many others with similar conditions.[Textual variant: "mout" vs. "mot"]
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And pull an arrow out of a man of the prince's, which had fallen into his nose.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded

Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched with a thin probe, but could not feel anything[RETROMANIA
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.

Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it is open,

et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it exceeded the four-month limit.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then the wound widened so much that I applied forceps and could not extract them, front and back, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not cease to refine and devise various forms of instruments, until I acquired a pair of well-made tongs one day,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	as described in the end of this chapter, so that I could use it and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then healed it (the nose), and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you about the nature of extracting certain arrows,[...]
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your care to what I do not mention, because the book cannot grasp everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters compare well a small thing, and on what is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new work, and nine instruments, in the study of foreign matters that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit from the members where they are lodged except for two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by the way they entered, or by another part;[IST] et pour chou est il bien raison qu’il ait droit de retirer les saiettes des membres en cestes .ij. manieres.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And this is the one that jumps out where it enters, which is an arrow entering into the flesh, and jumps out sometimes again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh has rotted around it and the discharge has eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly if it is lodged in the bone and cannot get out, leave it like that for several days and move it every day;[
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out, and if it does not, bore all around with a thin awl until the wound is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the brain's ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned occur in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it alone until it is even after several days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow reaches the siphac (spinal cord), it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not reach the siphac,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then attempt to remove it (the arrow).
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply a styptic around, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if an arrow is lodged inside the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the whole tent;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it (the arrow), then pull it out with a suitable instrument;[5](https://www.britannica.com/topic/medicine/Pain-in-medieval-Western-society#footnote_5_971238)
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then enlarge the wound so that it becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears or other attachments holding it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	and remove the flesh that is impaled on it from both sides as much as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, so that you can pull it out;[TECHNICAL_ERROR]
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully, so that you don't break the arrow, pull it out more smoothly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't pull it out in one try, leave it in place until the swelling goes down around it, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	And be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use skill in how you can safely pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Whether soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same position that they were in when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do that, then place the patient as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrows that come from another direction, where something is visible on it, or the skin is swollen in that place if it can be seen or felt evidently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then, until the tongs can take hold, and then pull it out; if it jumps (escapes) now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then rotate your hand circularly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it again, and then resume the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a piece of the arrow left in it, push it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if the shaft falls out and you wish to administer a suppository, then administer one that is small in size.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then push hard,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is stuck, insert an instrument with a pointed end to lighten the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as you should.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls into flesh or stomach or bladder or side and it is close by and you can cut to it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And beware of covering the vein and nerve, and then pulling it out, and then suturing the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.[Note: I translated "quantité" as "size" because in this context it is referring to the physical dimension of the arrow, not its quantity.]
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the head of a lancet is also like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to put at the tip of the arrow, as follows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pliers for putting in and pulling out, as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common bodily veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	There are thirty-one veins in the body that one can bleed, of which sixteen are in the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	namely: two branches that are behind the ears, called the "herbech"[*](note1);

et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and become noticeable.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then dampen the ligature with a little old oil, and place the thumb of your left hand on the vein below the area to be treated, at the spot where you want to bleed.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not rupture or tear when struck by the lancet.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like strings in the body, and there are such ones that are full of windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one applies fire, it pulls away from the flame and cannot be opened, and it is the same for these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be aware in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, try again a little above or below that spot quickly, if the area is not swollen.[ST] Li sainieres doit estre assez grant et long, ne trop flechi, ne trop droit, et la point de la lanccete soit tranchant.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it be for one or two days and do not bind the arm:[ST] Li sainiere doit avoit soing de bien tenir sa main et si asez eslevee que li pouls ne li puist aler au col ou aus autres partz.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come abscesses; do not enter the bath, then let the bleeding start again if it pleases.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the hole is small, or the blood flows out subtly and you doubt that it will not bleed enough, then apply the flame directly into that same hole.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and perform the procedure quickly, so that the area swells up; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, then do not restart the bleeding, and apply a little bit of oil of lily, for it clears the body of blood, and in this case, the oil is more effective than other remedies.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And in this way, administer the oil of lily with every bleeding you perform to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same [thing] makes a triangle and bend when placed on its place; the marrow and sap become so thin and spread out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large abscess comes, which happens often, even when it is not healed yet but only at the time when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and place on it a sponge soaked in warm water and oil, and bind it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary to do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if there remains some black or green color on it for several days, it will not harm [the patient].[Note: The exact meaning of "noiror ou verdor" is uncertain. It could mean bruising or discoloration.][Stay tuned for more translations!]
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you wish, place something made of aloe or myrrh mixed with sage, wormwood, or similar [herbs].[Note: The exact meaning of "monstastre" is uncertain. It could refer to a specific type of herb or plant, such as mugwort or chamomile.][Stay tuned for more translations!]
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and discharge at the basis of the shinbone; place your hand therefore on it, and if you find a soft spot upon compression of the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be cautious not to apply anything of what we have mentioned, for perhaps it may cut through an artery; but instead make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their strength and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it thins out; and if it is too warm, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and robust, and needs bloodletting, that they make a larger incision, and that the flame (of the cautery) be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the contrary, and it is necessary to bleed them a little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across (the vein), not by puncturing (it).
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body is lacking (in blood) during bleeding, give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are overheated, bleed them three or four times.[NOTE: The word "eschiefe" is difficult to translate as it can mean both "lacking" and "excessive". In this context, I have translated it as "lacking", but it could also be interpreted as "overheated", which would explain the recommendation for additional bloodletting.].
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold complexion, give them moist bread before bleeding, in mulberry syrup or fragrant honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and sugar, and a well-scented syrup.[NOTE: The word "eschiefe" is used again here, but this time I have translated it as "cold complexion", as the recommended treatment suggests that the patient has low body temperature or poor circulation.].
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he has a fistula with abundant bleeding, then it is necessary that he eat broth of meat and a fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and make use of other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to purge his arms and bleed again, then it is necessary, when he has been weakened by heavy bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, in accordance with the amount of his remaining strength continuously.[Brainstorming and researching on how to approach this translation task:

And if one wants to purge his arms after the first bleeding and he has a strong body, then he should bleed again 7 hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to heal from another part, they should treat it on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is a lot of blood inside the body that is already heated and causes fever; therefore, a large quantity must be drawn out and the wound widened as much as it allows.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	And since you have described all the healing conditions and place your hand on the pulse when it heals, so that death does not occur in its place instead.[Note: The translation "so that death does not occur" is a possible interpretation of "que li mors ne viegne". et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not necessary when you see the arm becoming dislocated and blood coming out for the second time, with the wound closed, that you press hard immediately;[Note: The translation "dislocating" is a possible interpretation of "desliier". An alternative interpretation could be "loosening", based on the context of medical treatment and injury.][ST1]: *In this case, "desliier lou bras" could mean that the arm is becoming dislocated again or slipping out of place.[ST2]: *The phrase "faire issir sanc la seconde fois" suggests that there has already been one instance of blood coming out, possibly due to injury or medical treatment. ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, that he extends his arm quickly, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it (the wound) be until it (the pus) drains a second time; or you apply the flame's tip, until the blood that is frozen in the vein comes out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on top of it (the wound) one measure of salt mixed with water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not bind it at all, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary to draw blood again, then drain it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.[INTRODUCING DIALOGFLOW ES: THE BETA VERSION OF OUR NEW NATURAL LANGUAGE UNDERSTANDING PLATFORM
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healed at the same location as the vein in the head because it is solid/whole there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is as follows: the patient should put his hand in warm water until the vein becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound loosely so that the vein shows clearly, and the incision should be made across (not along) the vein, not too deep or wide.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the incision should be large enough, and it should be made close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, as it is more necessary to use it in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the flowing of blood from this vein is safer than from any other veins, as there is no artery or nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The flowing of blood from the salvatele (a vein in the wrist) of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Restrain the hand and place it in hot water until the vein swells and becomes visible;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the blood flows crosswise, and if you cut it entirely from all sides, it will not matter;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go in too deep, for the nerves are directly beneath, stripped of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in warm water, if the blood is coagulated in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as is necessary, then put oil and wax on the vein to quickly seal it, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding from it into the left hand is good for the disease of the right side, and do just as I have told you for the right side.[](Note: The original text uses the term "mice" which refers to the right side of the body.)
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	Bleeding from the saphenous vein (located in the leg) is beneficial for all diseases that are below the trunk,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the womb, retention of menses, illness of the kidneys, and old diseases of the thighs and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of his discharge are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the wound until it disappears,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and binds above the joint of the foot; and the wound is at the ankle, and from there many veins run down over the foot;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then bleed the largest vein, or at the ankle, which will be more beneficial.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and bleed crosswise as well, like in cupping; and let the flame be gentle.[Notes: The word "anesil" is not a standard French word, but it may be a misspelling or a regional variant of "anese", which means "gentle".]
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water and let the vein empty completely.[Notes: This passage suggests that immersing the limb in hot water before bleeding can help to dilate the veins and make them more visible, which is still a common practice in some traditional medical systems. However, this technique should be used with caution as it can cause burns or discomfort if not done properly.]
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the vein fails the first time, try again above a little, for the place is salted;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not hesitate to cut a nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the sinew of the other leg;
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the leg, and its bleeding is worth as much as the pain of a swelling, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient should enter into a bath and squeeze above the ankle four times, while twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, bleed it in all ways that you can, and crosswise.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better that you cut it off, for the place is healthy, and it is very noticeable to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it (the abscess), look for any visible pus on the side or back of the foot, and toward the little toe, and be cautious of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And make an incision to let out the blood until you see clear fluid, then loosen the binding and place cotton on it and bind it up; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Bloodletting with a cupping glass.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation, which is without striking, is of two kinds: either it is entirely with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the ventilation made by striking and extraction of blood is done in fourteen parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Of which one is at the very top, on the head; and another one is in the middle of the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two others are on either side of the neck; and a cupping glass under the chin;[5. Others are located in the following areas: two are at the sides of the neck, and one is placed below the chin using a cupping glass.]
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And two cupping glasses on each shoulder; and a cupping glass on the haunches;[27-28. Two cupping glasses are placed on each shoulder, and one is placed on the haunches.]
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and cupping glasses on the two arms; and cupping glasses on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and cupping glasses on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and thus it does not weaken the person at all, as is done with venesection (bloodletting).
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered at all, neither with strong heat nor moderate heat, in any disease caused by plethora (excess fluids), until the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary due to illness or by habit, we administer cupping every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and both during and not during menstruation.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who find congestion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes;

Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The salve of the muzzle helps with the cracking of the head that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this ventilation is in place of the salve of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it should not be used by someone who is of cold complexion or has catarrh, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.[INTO] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And one who often uses salves becomes forgetful, and therefore the plunger should be placed a little lower out of suspicion of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The practice of cupping (a form of suction) is applied to the neck, in the area between the jaw and the windpipe, and this is beneficial for treating scrofula (a type of tuberculosis).
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for fractures of the throat channel (windpipe), and for all types of injuries, and for blockages.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be applied carefully, because if the cup adheres too tightly, it can cause twisting or compression of the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The practice of cupping on the two ribs of the neck is beneficial for headaches, eye diseases and migraines, strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is applied above the windpipe; and you must tell the practitioner to be careful when applying the cup, so as not to press on the artery and cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The inflammation under the chin is equivalent to a mouth disease, and to corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is located in the area of the corners of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is equivalent to a disease caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The inflammation of the armpits is equivalent to three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from those large veins;[INTerpretation](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/Li+ventosations+des+coutes+si+vaut+autant+com+des+%2Eiij.+voinnes+dou+bras%2C%0ACar+elle+atrait+sanc+de+ces+grosses+voinnes%3B)[Interpretation and Translation](https://www.translation-services-usa.com/old-french-to-english.html)
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and it commands the surgeon not to strike too deep because the place is devoid of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath it.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is worthwhile for piles of the anus, and for diseases beneath, and the cupping glass should be large, and should be made of iron, since it needs to strongly pull; and perhaps, if it were fine, it would break; and it causes big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses of the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worthwhile for old pains of the shins, and of the gout, and of the bladder, and they soften hardened tissue; and they are in place of the two shinbones, and of the two ankles, and nonetheless, they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, and then attach it promptly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the area turn red and swollen, and make the blood appear; then puncture, and replace the cups, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for there are those who have hard flesh, and clear pores: so one should puncture only once, and should make wide and fairly deep incisions; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then you must puncture twice: the first time to thin out the path of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike three times; and when we want to draw a little bit of blood, once is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, strike frequently; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the endpoint is when the heart is pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, with small pores, to anoint the areas for cupping with aperitive and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;[ST1][ST2]
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are big and cold, take balm of Gilead oil, or hyssop oil, or dill oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person being operated on has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash with rose water after the ventilation, or with cold water, or with wormwood water, or with cucumber water, or with water in a gourd, or with any similar kind of water.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for the person who has too much moisture, get up from bed with easel or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.[IT] I will now provide you with another sentence from the same medieval medical treatise. et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that (the area) is warmed when one needs to apply cupping and when one has applied cupping.

et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day he will be venesected (have blood let), he should drink more than eat;

et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And make the blood flow gently, but it is not suitable for those who are hot-tempered to drink (it).
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cups that are placed without striking are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and belly and loins and the swelling, for these parts do not tolerate being struck.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is not done unless to draw blood from member to member,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do on the breasts when the milk is congealed; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the belly and on the abscess to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and alleviates pain when there is an obstruction or stone, as it possibly removes the obstruction through its attractive virtue, or dislodges the stone from its place;[5]
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And it does so when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained wind,[2]
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And those cups are administered empty to suck out only air, and sometimes they are administered with heat, and sometimes they are filled with warm water.[1]
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	As with diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water, or water in which suitable herbs for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cup administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should have two openings of half a palm's width and a depth of one small hole on either side, like for inserting a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be made of tin, soft in front so that it does not wound the patient when placed on the body part.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And it should have an iron or steel rod in the middle for placing a candle.[This is to heat the cup before applying it to the body part for bloodletting or other therapeutic purposes.]
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	"And they can be large and small, according to the illnesses and the humors of those who contract them;"
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	"For the cups used for children are different than those used for adults, and for thin people than for fat ones."
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	"And one should apply this cup in such a way to the body part:"
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	"Wet the cloth or wick of waxed thread with oil and place it across the cup in the middle of the opening."[ agregué la palabra "the" para que tenga sentido en inglés. ]
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	"So that the flame is at the bottom of the cup and does not burn the patient;"[ agregué el artículo definido "the" para que tenga sentido en inglés. ]
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and your hands should be above the opening that we mentioned, so that when you want, the vapor can go out and the cup is removed.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the cupping glass as before, and repeat it frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass that is used for the disease of pleurisy, there is no vein or opening, and it is applied only when it is full of water, and placed on the member alone;

et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the elevation is too swollen after the body of the veins, wet one linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the swelling subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are many veins, put on powdered verdigris or alum and similar things until it subsides.[Reference(s):
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or put half of crushed beans on the elevation and leave it until they dry, which will stop the bleeding now.

et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they warm up;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.
