Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the repair of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish miraclesed people throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read a letter (of them).
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the science is strange in our land, as I never found any good (examples) of it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except for the knowledge from ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered it, and through experience, and through the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in these two chapters before;
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is thus necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his attention, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or crushing comes upon anyone, it is necessary to quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if no obstacle prevents it, such as weakness of the body, infants, or the elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the season is not very hot or too cold; and similarly for cold foods, that is to say cold meats such as chicken and goat meat, and let them not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill their stomachs with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain there is no danger of hot abscess or spreading matter to the limb; so let the patient return to their usual regimen that they had before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for thick nourishment, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and dairy products, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For through proper care, deformities and fractures are healed more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the elderly and infirm cannot heal or knit together properly due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but it does not matter, set a large splint on the broken bone which holds and brings the limb together, as long as it heals as before; and do not disturb his work at all, and therefore he must be fed with rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse and varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the skull is different than that of the ribs or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes toward the armpit, and another one pointing, like the cut of a pen's feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type should have its own tool and proper instrument in restoration, according to what comes to mind (memory) in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the break of the bone is recognized by this: that the place is twisted, and it is clear from the outside, and it sounds when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist or swelling in the touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, nor is there any fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But there may be a twist, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	And you should not move it by hand, but apply the following medications and then bind it gently.[Read More](https://www.engrade.com/browse/essay-topic-generator?title=Ancient+Medicine)
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks in the limbs, where the two parts are separated, you should bring them into alignment and make sure they are evenly placed, so that pus does not form.[Read More](https://www.engrade.com/browse/essay-topic-generator?title=Ancient+Medicine)
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if pus does form, let it be for some days until the abscess subsides.[Read More](https://www.engrade.com/browse/essay-topic-generator?title=Ancient+Medicine)[SIMILAR ARTICLES](https://www.engrade.com/browse/essay-topic-generator?title=Ancient%2BMedicine)
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it evenly in the joint that you can easily and skillfully reduce, and know that the restoration of the former is easier than the restoration of the latter where there are broken parts; then bind it, as is appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it with two parts, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb back in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, you bring together all the additions in their places with all means possible, and make sure that through your work, the patient does not suffer injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and align well the two ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And they can feel it with their hand if it doesn't seem to be in place: then straighten it nicely and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring about a hot and constricted abscess in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, admonish the patient well not to move it, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure that the limb is so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed, and you must put it in such a position that they feel no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And take care that it is set straight, so that there will be no deformity when it is healed.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	"And the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you."
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	"For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: these must be wrapped with soft and fine linen."[2](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/drapel#fr)
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	"And those that are large, such as hips and legs: these must be wrapped with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the entire large member and constrain it equally from all sides so that there is no slack."[2](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/liien#fr)
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	"Then wrap it with light bandages, three or four turns depending on the member, and tighten your hand a little on all the bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture is slightly separated."[2](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/estoupe#fr)[2](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/tour#fr)
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take another ligament, and turn it again around the broken joint;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the area below the break, and gently tighten it, not too tight or too loose, as we have said in the first section mentioned above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place linen or cloth wadding between the ligaments until they are even, then bind it all with a bandage, and then put your well-made irons on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, place something warm that reduces the abscess and removes the swelling on it, and leave it like that for several days;[SPS. The following text is from a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then apply pressure on your belt, and let the bleeding be half as much as the width of a reed, or from a piece of wood used for making roof tiles, or from palm leaves, and let it be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the belt placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is needed for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then apply pressure on the belts as you did in the first application, then tie a string appropriately on top of it, just as in the first application on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and make it tighter, and less so each time; and the string should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made from soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their sutures with twisted linen thread, and this is a great error, for the stitch cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than the width of a finger's breadth between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the ends of the stitches after tightening in healthy places, place under them lint or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bones are broken, I will tell you the treatment as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to tighten with stitches all the fractured members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not suitable to put in stitches except after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of abscess happening;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Here is the method of ancient emplasters to heal fractures, dislocations, and twisting: it consists of taking flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mixing it well with a large amount of egg, then using this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and applying it in this way. This is the common method of the restorative emplaster for healing fractures in various ways, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of the restorative emplaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take three parts of costmary, ladanum, elecampane, asafoetida, gum arabic, and myrrh; each part is ten drams; and four drams each of myrrh and aloes; and grind them into a powder, then mix with egg yolk; if the person's complexion is hot, use this emplaster as it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of the emplaster that is good for twisting: take myrrh and colt's foot, each ten drams; four drams each of aloes and acacia, eight drams of Armenian bole, grind well, and mix with water or egg yolk, then administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of poultice for joints and dislocated bones, to calm the resulting pain, and for healing broken bones: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the spot. This poultice does not heal completely, but it is good for cooling down hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed broad-leaved thyme, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of poultice for the healing of bone fractures and reducing the remnants of abscesses: take root of althea, chamomile, violet flowers, bran, an equal amount of each; grind, mix with wine, and if the member is warm, moisten it with coriander water or plain water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger poultice than the previous one, when hard abscesses come to restore the member: take root of althea, seeds of flax, balm, sweet clover, violet flowers and chamomile, an equal amount of all; grind, mix with water of salt or plain water or with wine, depending on the warmth of the member and its rest.[ST1]
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not place anything on the broken member to restore it, except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderate in hardness, not too soft or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place on the broken member, to restore it, dry and slightly warm things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another form of poultice that is good for wounds and pain: take a dog's mouth and chopped off men's hair, or bird feathers, and chamomile, and equally, grind them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little after, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain or if the bone has not moved from its place, and do not unbind it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and unbind it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge, and dip in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed down.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, wet with water or rose oil, and bind it to a compress, until you are sure of a heated abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be removed, then begin the binding again, more lightly, and a little poultice, and do not bind it as tight as before; and carefully, until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the heated and red abscess and pain and swelling have all been removed, and you need poultice and bandages, then begin again as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if the member does not come to any of what we have said, do not unlock it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, so that the breaker is careful, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh on top;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then restrain it more than before, and the flesh swells, as I said before; and if you see the place dry out more than necessary, know that healing cannot come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Therefore, it arises from hot wet swelling every time you unlock it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the binding a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work, healing is delayed in the member, and it heals slowly what foolish surgeons do, who incorrectly set the member; this is bad, and it is a practice to be feared, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and their causes are differentiated;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by sword blows, and the collarbone separates the entire bone down to the syphac which is beneath the bone, just like a hatchet or stick; and this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword strikes the bone from above without penetrating, this type of fracture is called "absolue"; and the wound of these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a chip fracture, or a stone collar, or falling on a stone, or other similar things;
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture that reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is sunken into the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "hairline" or "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or from similar causes, and it drives a piece of bone inward, and the place is uneven, like when coopers hammer on cauldrons; it goes inside the body.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more frequently in those who have moist bones in their head, such as the bones of children.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs in all types of fractures where small pieces are detached, like so; and I will speak about it further on.[ST1] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the withdrawal (traction) on them, and the investigation using tensors, and by the decayed flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	A fracture is recognized by the appearance of hair when, after uncovering the bone and rubbing over it, a black line becomes visible.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be aware of the patient's condition and if you notice any adverse symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paleness, feverish chills, eyes turning out and becoming red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it is unlikely to heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.[nitpicky]
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when a wounded person first comes to you in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month if possible.[nitpicky]
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the joint, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become rotten, and the complications that we mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane covering the brain, then you must cut open the split part in this way: that is, take hold of the head of the injured patient, and expose the bone as much as you can, in the shape of the wound as gently as possible.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if bleeding occurs when the bone is exposed or an abscess arises, then help as appropriate and that is to fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil.[*](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/roset)
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess has healed and you are sure that there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, and this can be done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and its shape is: ... (the text goes on to describe the incision)
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put in another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and firm, then you must pierce it all around, so that you administer cuts with trephines, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the thickness of the skull, and there should be above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the tip to pass beyond the bone; and you need several of them, so that each one comes to rest in its place on the surface of the bone, so that you have trephines for all parts of the head; and this is the method of the three types of trephines.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The way to pierce around the bone is to place a trephine on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is penetrated; then remove the trephine and place it in another spot nearby, and do this all around, then cut out the space of the skull between the holes with a chisel, doing this as delicately as possible and lightly, as we have said, so that you extract the bone by hand or with any of the tools that you have such as pliers or forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have penetrated and extracted the bone, then it is necessary that you clean the sharpness that remains from the bone with another tool resembling a chisel, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there remains any fragments of small bones or splinters, then carefully remove them with one of the instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it highly, and this is his statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, it is necessary to uncover a portion of the bone in the place where the fracture is clearly visible. Once you have exposed that area, place the rounded tip of this surgical knife under the edge, as shown in its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not make a cut all the way through on one side, rather leave it jagged in two edges so that the blade is alongside the bone. Then strike gently with a small mallet to lightly break the bone all around, taking great care of the cloth underneath.[...]
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is loose from the bone, then remove it gently, for it can be easily removed without harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break of the bone does not penetrate through to the outer layer, and the bone is only cut through at the top, with small pieces, then you must smooth over that roughness, and remove the splinters with a sharp razor which you should have in various quantities, to make suitable adjustments in each place, according to the task and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use large razors, then smaller ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircutters and subtle breakers, it is necessary to make adjustments according to its alignment; and this is something that is not obvious to one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the abscess is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound and soak it in rose oil and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another cloth, doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another bandage on top, but don't pull it tight, just enough to hold the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down, then loosen the bandage and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetches flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these and sprinkle it on the wound, then continue to apply painless medicine.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and make sure that the wound stays clean, not allowing any pus to accumulate or for it to become infected, because if pus forms under the cloth on the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; this is because when a painful substance is placed on the abscess, it causes necrosis.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any accident should befall the patient, as we have mentioned, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no pus comes out unless due to the medicine that has been applied, which has such power, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and glue one bandage, and place it on the styptic.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it in various ways until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or twists, and then heals.[Zapier generated this text automagically]
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your little finger or the tip of your nose into the nostril and push the breakage inside with your index finger until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the knee, and the bone cannot come into place, then you should align it even with the end of a rod that is slightly thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, then do likewise (i.e. align it with a rod), and make haste to set it in place on the first day, if you are able;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has healed, then insert into the end of the knee tendons made of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one piece.[Note: The translation "tentes de drapelz de lin" could also be rendered as "strips of linen fabric".]
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert one (tent) from the other side if the fracture is there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the hole(s) of the knee.[Note: The phrase "les pertus dou neis" could also be rendered as "the openings of the knee".]
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some healer(s) say that one must moisten the tendons with butter and change them daily. But I do not think this is a good idea; rather, they should be moistened with egg white and powdered mallow during their preparation, and then leave the tendon until the bone is hard and the cartilage has toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes, one puts goose feathers in place of tenting, and with a soft cloth around, and the assistant holds it in place, and the patient blows through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses or pustules come on the nose while you are working, put on cerote (a type of medication) or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a patch of diachylon (an adhesive plaster).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if no abscesses come, apply an emplaster from outside, made of chamomile flour, and incense powder, combined with egg white, then put light wicks on top, but do not bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break of the nose is small and it is broken into many pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then sew up the incision, and cure it with remedies for healing flesh, and soldering, such as plasters and ointments suitable for that.[translation] The text describes the medical treatment for a broken or injured nose. If the break is small and the nose is broken into many pieces, the physician should extract the pieces using appropriate instruments. After that, the physician should sew up the incision and apply remedies to help heal the flesh and bind the wound, such as plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then cure it with tenting and put in splints of wood until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured but there is no wound outside, and the break is external only, without being broken in two, except for a small piece inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, then you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left side, then insert your right hand's index finger, gently push the fracture inside, and align it with the other hand from the outside, making sure they are equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer extension to both sides until they are equal.[SIMULATE] Me: How did medieval medical practitioners diagnose a fractured jawbone?
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a break, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a compress on the broken jaw, and place on it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide to the jaw, and tie it to the chin as best you can, and command the patient to rest, and feed them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, then untie it on the third day, and then set right what has changed; and place a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the compress; and place a light linen cloth on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, then use what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine if any piece of bone has been removed from it; then carefully remove it with the appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all those pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound if it is large, and apply a suitable poultice to it, to help heal the flesh until it is healed.

Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is when there is no wound in the break: that you have two assistants, so that one holds the support that feels the broken forceps; and the other stretches out the neck towards the part; then place the fracture evenly between your hands, so that the form is as it should be, without any appearance or unevenness.[INST
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, place below the patient's shoulder a round cushion of fabric or wool, and make it as thick as necessary; extend and lift the limb, and press the cushion with your hand, so that you align the break evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the limb out straight, because it goes too deep, then the patient must lie on his side and place a medium-sized cushion under his shoulder, and the assistant should push the shoulder down until the bone of the limb is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the break with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, then saw across; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bones cannot join because of any obstacle, then cut one of the fragments off with the instrument that you have; but place the cushion underneath the limb to protect the soft tissue.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and let it be shaped like a spoon, but not too sharp, and make it as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the operation; and have two holes in it, as you see, one wide and one narrow, corresponding to the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, then bandage the wound with linen cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, wet one linen cloth in rose oil, vinegar, and essential oil, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is to place the emplaster of mill powder and egg white on the bone, and then place light cotton swabs on top, and place a sponge underneath if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then place a double cloth on the swabs and the emplaster; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around this bandage, leaving the ends of the bandage hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck and under the healthy and injured asselles (?) and massage each part. And when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the binding loosens, tighten it again.[EXTEND\_ANSWER] The text describes a method for treating a fractured bone using a stick and bandages. The stick is placed on top of the fracture, and then the bandages are wrapped around the neck and under the asselles (a body part that is not clear from the text), both healthy and injured. The practitioner is instructed to massage each part and check if the ligature is holding the fracture properly. If it is, and the stick is not moving above the broken bone, then the bandages should be rewrapped every day. Additionally, when the binding loosens, it should be tightened again.

puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the poultice if you see that it is necessary, and bind it and leave it like that until they are healed; and it is healed in at most 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates in such a way that it can be seen from the outside; one only knows this through touch. One should prepare the treatment according to the type of break and reposition it according to its natural shape, in all ways possible. Then put powdered flour mixed with egg white and light sponges on top, then a double layer of cloth. After that, place a wide and thin board over it, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the board, fill them with linen sponges so that the board lies flat. Then bind it firmly all around with a long bandage, making sure that the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day. And whenever it softens, tighten it again and make sure the board is in the right place, and have the patient lie on their side. The shoulder should be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is reached, untie it, and be careful because it is not an easy thing for the bone to come out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breakage of the forearm to pacify a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the break of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of strength, and soon, and perhaps they vomit blood, and the fracture can be seen in the broken bone, and one can smell it easily.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is as follows: the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then you should press their shoulders and bring together their ribs using your hands, making sure to align all parts of the bone correctly; afterwards, apply poultices and bandages soaked in saltwater or another light wood over the fracture, wrap it in a cloth, and secure it firmly over the broken bone so that it does not move; then tie a bandage around their back, tighten it appropriately, and check every hour to see if it needs to be tightened again; if it becomes necessary to loosen the bandage due to infection, itching, pain, or abscess, do so quickly, remove the poultice, treat the affected area as needed, reapply a new poultice, and secure it until healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination of the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the setting consists of aligning the break properly, as is appropriate. Then apply the emplaster and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of ribs leans inward, then the patient feels great pain and distress, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the skin; and there is sharp pain when breathing, and immediately there is a large flow of blood, which is a serious matter. Ancient physicians have applied much skill to this problem.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one must administer food that causes the belly to swell in order to push the break outward.[0](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/aministrer)
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to a head, then lance it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should apply cups to the place in order to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the place due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the place with a cloth soaked in hot oil and then place bandages between the ribs to evenly apply pressure around, and then let it be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pressing against the cloth, and if the patient is anxious, then you must make an incision on the place where the rib is broken, and place a device underneath to protect the lung; and then you should cut the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it heals. And if an abscess comes, then put wet bandages soaked in rose oil on the area, and place them on the patient; and treat the place as one does for an abscess, and keep the patient lying on their side on the rib where they must lie, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the break/fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a break/fracture in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, look to see if you notice their hands are softened, swollen, and without feeling, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that in many cases, this means they are mortally injured, but if they can move them and feel when they are pressed or poked, know that the joints of the bone are safe, and that the patient will recover if treated.[Reference(s):
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar things happen in the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will recover or not, look to see if the feet are soft, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when it is turned onto its stomach, there is still involuntary evacuation. And when it is turned onto its back and wants to sit up, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not even attempt to cure it.[Reference(s):
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then it is a less severe condition.[Reference(s):
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you should do if there is a hot abscess, place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is calmed down; then place one of the warming and drying plasters on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the area with a compress; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then cure it with a healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", place your left hand pocket on it, and push it into place with your right hand to the best of your ability, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, adjust it and remove it, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the thigh bone is broken, and if it does, it rarely results in much narrowing at the end; it bends long and inclines outward, and causes pain to the patient in that area, and swelling and bruising in the area where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or angulated inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that you can align the restoration of that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice, and place a stick or wooden peg on top of it, holding the break in place so that it does not move; and apply a bandage beneath the ribs, until the swelling is equalized.[`json
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come from it, do not touch it until the arising abscess has calmed down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if no bad accident occurs; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint breakage
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what lies between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a rod of medium size, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the shoulder joint with two bandages and pull them upwards, and place the patient on a seat; then let him rest his broken arm on the rod, so that it is in the middle of a bow-shaped piece of wood, then suspend it from some heavy object or have the attendant stretch it downward; then bring the two ends of the break together with your hands until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to position the patient on his backside, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold either end of the broken bone with their hands, one holding the part above the break, and the other holding the part below, each pulling in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tie one ligament below the break and another above it, and have each assistant pull in their direction. And if the break is close to the top of the shoulder, place one ligament in the middle below the armpit, and another towards the side, below the break; and do the same if the break is towards the side. Then align the break as it should be, and apply even tension, if no abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do form, then do not apply tension for seven days, and place a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil on the affected area. Wait until the abscess has calmed down, then apply tension. The method of applying tension is to place the poultice on the break, align the arm with the shoulder or chest, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest. Then place a cloth and apply tension on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm remains in its natural position, if nothing prevents it, and unless the bones are misaligned.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bones are misaligned, use a splint and place a wider and stronger rod over the break than the others, with a space of two fingers between each rod. Each rod should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side. Then apply tension to the rods as I described at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less gradually.[Additional context: This passage describes the use of a splint to stabilize and align a fractured bone before applying tension.]
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound up until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days to see if itching, inflammation, or discharge comes to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. Loosen it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not loosen it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool underneath them. Look every hour of the day and night to see if the shape of the broken member changes or if the binding has become too loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give the patient the food that we mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially fine; and when they begin to recover, make it coarse. And it is customary for the binding and leg to be recovered in 40 days in total; and then one should unbind and administer baths and ointment medications to straighten the place. And if the stricture is severe and embedded, then delay unbinding for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Here's the translation of the text you provided in Old French about the treatment for a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosicles", one of which is small and is the one that follows the thumb; and the other is large and is the one that is below, towards the little finger; it may happen that only the large fosicle breaks, or only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.
